> I might take a little peek again to see if FreeBSD has changed as much as I

Probably not.  I think it's great, but FreeBSD isn't for everyone.  The 
documentation is still too sparse, and while I have never noticed any 
specific newbie-unfriendliness on the mailing lists I follow, that may be 
because I'm not a newbie.  It's not an OS I'd recommend to anyone with 
lots of multimedia toys or cutting-edge hardware, but that's not an issue 
for me - what I do care about is stability, speed, system transparency, 
and customizability.  And robust software install & upgrades.

> Monday, October 31, 2005, 8:31:48 PM, you wrote:

> DL> On Mon, 2005-10-31 at 17:09 -0800, AthlonRob wrote:
> >> David Tod Sigafoos wrote:
> >> > BUT .. not all distros work with hardware.  I used Fedora 4 because it
> >> > is known to work with HP Laptops (specifically the zd8000 line).  Wait
> >> > .. there is another problem .. Linux doesn't work on all or even most
> >> > boxes.  And a distro that works on one doesn't necessarily work on
> >> > another.
> >> 
> >> Actually, with a bit of work any piece of hardware that works on one
> >> distro will work on any other distro.  Hardware is controlled by the
> >> kernel... and it's Linux all around.  :-)
> 
> DL> Only if you can install the OS far enough to recompile the kernel.  If
> DL> the default kernel won't install the OS, then its time to look for
> DL> another.
> 
> recompile the kernel .. i am sorry but i gave up that with the other
> childish toys of my youth <G>
> 
> I love to play with stuff .. but usually it is how to may my apps the
> best apps they can be .. how to bring new features to users and how to
> create new 'tools' in the environment for developers.
> 
> It isn't to spend lots of time recompiling kernels for searching for
> missing bits of an application someone has placed out there.  <g>
> 
> DL> FWIW, I've had more success with Debian than any other installer, but
> DL> only because the Debian installer allows you to take control of just
> DL> about every aspect of the installation process.  This installer is not
> DL> good for newbies, but the defaults should get most systems up and
> DL> running.
> 
> When you grap an XP disk or server 2003 disk .. you stuff it in ..
> press the button and off you go.  Oh yeah .. you have to know what
> region you are in but other than that  .. BANG BIFF POW you have a
> system that knows EVERYTHING about your hardware.

Obviously you haven't done that many windows installs, I've only ever
had that happen a few times, most of the other time, drivers had to be
tracked down, and a large number of times the install didn't work as
advertised causing more hair loss (mainly because the error messages
make no sense) trying to get it working.  Some drivers have to be loaded
during the install (mostly RAID controllers), and windows is so
antiquated that you still HAVE to use the floppy drive to load them.  A
large number of machines out there come with no floppy drive!
> 
> I love to hear the 'recompile kernel' bit <G>
> 
> Now i know that Linux isn't there yet (kernel or os or distro or ..
> pick your definition) and am ok with a bit of blood on the finger
> nails and a waste of a lot of time.  But I wonder if it will change
> when all the mails i have gotten do not critically look at Linux ..
> (kernel, distro, os or what ever) and see what need to be done about
> making it a more acceptable solution.

Since I am not a developer, I only look at what can be done with what is
out there now.  I have had the same load of Debian unstable for about 5
years now, it has not always worked 100%, but I have always been able to
fix it.  I have changed motherboards three times, video cards about five
times and have added and subtracted all kinks of peripheral hardware.
In the same time period I have had to reload windows at least a half
dozen times, talk about a monumental waste of time!

Anyway, I would rather take the time to recompile to a leaner faster
kernel that will be around for years than to have to deal with the
bizarre ways that Bill has found to screw up an OS.

If your lively hood is dependent on billable hours, then I would not
recommend using linux.  Windows will most definitely keep the customers
calling back.  This is kind of a strange industry, happy customers are
not the ones that keep calling back, they are the ones that have no
problems and only need to call you when they want to make changes.  This
leads to fewer billable hours per customer.

I feel your pain.

Derek Loree

On 11/1/05, Michael H. Collins <mike at linuxlink.com> wrote:
> If grub is set up correctly it should ask if you want win or lin.
> Unless I am missing the point of all this.

I think Chris wants to be able to type a magic command in Linux, walk
away, and come back to a Windows boot.  lilo's -R option lets you
change the default for the next boot (Windows) without changing the
normal default (Linux).

Jason

On Mon, Oct 31, 2005 at 09:33:25PM -0800, Russ Gilman-Hunt wrote:
> Ok, running Debian ( etch ) at home. This is just sort of a _general_
> question;
> 
> If I install sendmail from apt-get, and then spamassassin from apt-get,
> does sendmail then use spamassassin?

Nope.  You'll still have to tell your mail system how to actually
pass mail through spamassassin.  The package's author wouldn't want
to presume, after all.  ;)

Me, I just use a procmail rule instead of installing SA sitewide.  
If I were just doing it on a desktop, I'd use a Spamassassin proxy
(google for it) or Evolution's built-in Spamassassin support.  See:
http://software.newsforge.com/software/05/07/01/1521254.shtml?tid=130

And unless you already have a special affinity for Sendmail, I implore
you to use Exim (Debian's default MTA) or Postfix (another popular
MTA).  It's much easier to configure them.

> Is this answer pretty much the same across the board? Ie, if I apt-get
> apache2 and then apt-get php5 and then apt-get mysql4, will I be able to
> write my LAMP applications using this setup, or is there something I'll
> have to configure or compile?

It depends on whether there's only one obvious way to hook it up (I
think PHP5 + Apache is in this category.)  If there's a bunch of
reasonable ways to do it (e.g. Spamassassin can be configured for
several different MTAs, as a proxy, as an individual filter or for
sitewide operation) then the package author will leave it to you, the
Mighty Sysadmin, to figure out where the tentacles and squeaky bits go.


-- 
"All software grows until it can send and receive e-mail, not because
 this is a useful function, but because by becoming an MTA it can be
 complete in its suckfulness."  -- Anthony de Boer

On Tue, 1 Nov 2005, Rich Shepard wrote:
>  Do you know that there's an addition to Slackware that allows the use of
> the NetBSD port system? I don't feel the need to go that route, but it was
> suggested to me by an application developer in The Netherlands when I had
> problems with his installer not installing the rc file. A simple 'touch'
> fixed the problem and it works just fine now.


Nope, didn't know that.  Does Slackware have a package management system 
these days?  I (obviously) haven't been keeping up.

The ports system is pretty neat - it really can fix a lot of the 
dependency hell issues that rpm's are prey to - the only drawback is that 
there can be a fair amount of compilation involved, so it helps to have a 
reasonably fast machine.  Upgrading / recompiling the base system on my 
IM/DNS/time server (a 10-yr old HP Pentium 100) takes about 24 hours.
But most of the work can be run by a cron job, so you're not wasting your 
time while the system is checking, fetching, & recompiling your stuff.

--
David Fleck
david.fleck at mchsi.com

unsuccessfully trying to install kstars on my spouse's SuSE 9.1 machine. 
It turned out I needed to upgrade the machine's version of KDE, which I 
did, and most everything seems fine... but now when I minimize running 
windows, they simply vanish - the apps are still running, I can see them 
in 'ps', but they disappear from the GUI completely.  No, they're not off 
on another desktop, nor obscured by the taskbar or other running windows - 
they're just gone, irretrievably, until the user logs off and back on, at 
which time KDE dutifully resurrects all the old windows.  This problem 
doesn't appear in fvwm or other window managers.  Clearly, something's 
gotten screwed up in KDE, but I'm not familiar enough with it to figure 
out what.

Can someone  with greater familiarity with KDE help me figure out what's 
going on here?  Thanks.

<Slightly off-topic>

I am working on some instructions for students of linguistics 
regarding IPA fonts available, how to install them, and how to use 
them, including the good points and the bad points of each. The 
instructions will include Windows, Linux and Mac, and common 
applications on those platforms. Ideally I can post these on a wiki 
somewhere, then professors can point their students to the wiki. 

Does anyone know of a free and stable wiki where I can post these 
instructions? (Stable, as in "the site won't disappear in a couple of 
weeks when the person who started it loses interest.")

Google turned up a lot of wikis but they all seem to be commercial. 
I've read a lot of wikis, but this is the first time I've wanted to post 
on one. Any suggestions welcome.

Subject: [PLUG] Free wikis?
In-Reply-To: <20051102213530.GE17410@bavariati.org>
References: <4368B24B.26151.B2BC2D0@localhost>
Message-ID: <43692FE4.5386.D166153@localhost>

On 2 Nov 2005, at 13:35, Aaron Burt wrote: 

> Any particular reason to use a Wiki rather than a regular ol' static
> webpage in your school or home webspace?  (I can think of some--easy
> maintenance, can be handed off to another maintainer etc. but I'm
> curious what your thinking is.)

Because I don't know all the answers. I want several pages of 
information about the various free/pay fonts available, plus 
instructions on installing and using them on Linux, Windows and 
Mac, and then information on how to use them in various apps. I 
want something where the reader can edit the wiki to add his or her 
own information to the original. For example, I've never used a Mac. 
I'm going to have to leave that part blank for the moment because I 
have no idea how to install a font on a Mac. (And from talking to 
linguistics majors here, none of the Mac users knows either.) So 
hopefully a Mac user can add a paragraph or two about that issue. 

Because I want the reader to be able contribute, a wiki seemed the 
most appropriate venue.

From ehem at m5p.com  Wed Nov  2 22:50:50 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Wed, 2 Nov 2005 22:50:50 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] debian packages question
In-Reply-To: <20051101185752.C9C8B44D4@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200511030650.jA36ool2038825@m5p.com>

Hmm, seems I got behind on things.


>From: Aaron Burt <aaron at bavariati.org>
> And unless you already have a special affinity for Sendmail, I implore
> you to use Exim (Debian's default MTA) or Postfix (another popular
> MTA).  It's much easier to configure them.

I'd strongly advise avoiding Exim. Given how good the packaging is I'm
disgusted that Debian continues to use Exim as the default. I doubt
Postfix is any more difficult with the packaging that has been done.
Though Exim /might/ be easier to setup, it most definitely isn't easier
to maintain. Notably Exim tends to requires security updates every 2-3
months, Sendmail and Postfix need updates around once a year.

Heck, with the packaging even Qmail isn't too bad to deal with.

>From: Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>
> Now there's some flame bait. :-) Just to let you know that not 
> everyone thinks as Aaron does, the first thing I do on Debian systems 
> is ditch exim for sendmail. Unless you have a very vanilla setup, 
> configuring either one takes homework.

I agree. Even for pretty simple setups I have to imagine Postfix doesn't
need significantly more work than Exim. I cannot be certain though as I
haven't fought Postfix.

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Thu Nov  3 06:02:52 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Thu, 3 Nov 2005 06:02:52 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] palm devices
In-Reply-To: <200511021249.39756.mharrisdmd@earthlink.net>
References: <200511021249.39756.mharrisdmd@earthlink.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511030558240.4671@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Wed, 2 Nov 2005, Michael D. Harris wrote:

> I would like to order a palm device.  I noticed that in the specs on many
> of these devices Linux is not mentioned as an operating system that can be
> used to sync your device. Does anyone have any experience using the palm
> tools on Debian Linux (Sarge) to sync their Palms and does it require geek
> status to get it going?

Mike,

   We've used jpilot on the desktop since Judd first released it years ago.
The connection is via pilot-link which should be part of every distribution.
Over the years I've sync'd a Palm Persona, Professional, III, m105,
Handspring Visor Pro, and Kyocera QCP-6035 with nary a problem. If the PDA
runs a Palm OS, pilot-link and jpilot work just fine. We use both serial and
USB connections.

   Sometimes you have to add the users to the group owning the port, or you
can change the port's owner to yourself if you're the only user.

Rich

>
Make sure you aren't running over 60 hz refresh. Also, max resolution 
appears to be 1280x1024.

Russ

From rsteff at comcast.net  Thu Nov  3 13:47:48 2005
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Thu, 03 Nov 2005 13:47:48 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Comcast & Dealing with Unsolicited e-mail
Message-ID: <436A8584.9000606@comcast.net>

A few days ago I commented on e-mail I was getting with no subject, no 
sender, and no body text. The rate kept rising to the point where 
yesterday I was getting several every hour. I logged onto the Comcast 
e-mail system on the web and re-read what is offered for spam 
protection, hoping for a black list. Alas, there is none. Plus, their 
white list is an exclusive one: if you use it, you will only get e-mail 
from senders on the list. I asked them about it through their web site 
and got this as part of the reply:

----------------------------------------------------------------------
Thank you for taking the time to provide us with your suggestion on how 
to improve our service with the popular suggestion of a "black list" 
type of mail filter. Yes other subscribers have also requested it and it 
is a popular request. We may have that feature with our mail in the 
future, but we did not have a time of if or when it could become 
available. I have forwarded your suggestion to the appropriate 
management team for further review and action. We appreciate your 
interest in making the Comcast High Speed Internet the best online 
experience possible.
----------------------------------------------------------------------

I have been forwarding junk e-mail to missed-spam at comcast.net but it 
doesn't seem to have helped. If anything, the more I send them, the more 
junk mail I get!

One of the annoyances related to sending junk to missed-spam is having 
to do so one message at a time. So yesterday, I tried something 
different. I shut down T-bird for a few hours. Then, I logged onto the 
Comcast web mail system, checked all the above described junk mail (no 
subject...) and clicked on the "Report as Spam" button. I haven't gotten 
any of that kind of junk mail since. Maybe it's a coincidence, since 
they were doing some work on the e-mail system yesterday, but I'm a 
happier camper, today. We'll see how long that lasts.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens
http://home.comcast.net/~rsteff/

Note Cards & Photographic Prints available at:
http://home.comcast.net/~rcsphoto/

Ah, but there's a subtle difference here.

They are all using the same kernel. So they all CAN use the same 
hardware. The difference being how the distribution chooses to compile 
the kernel.

If the distibution chooses to not include a section of code, that's the 
distibutions decision (and fault), not the kernels.

>Now you may ask why it stops and get out your propeller and try to
>figure it out .. but i gave all that up years ago.  I want it to load.
>work and let me work.  Every hour spent trying to get it to work is an

>  
>
I agree. As long as the installer (created by the distribution, not the 
kernel maintainer) doesn't support your hardware, you have a problem. 
This is a problem by your choice, but it's still a problem.

I also realize that as long as computers don't work like toasters, there 
will be hardware that takes work to get to use. This is true even in the 
Windows world.

As I was commenting to someone just the other day...

There are those computer users that like to insert a CD, click 'Next' as 
fast as they can, as many times as needed, and it just works. Those are 
the same people that like Windows, and deal with instability as a result.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Thu Nov  3 18:16:04 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Thu, 3 Nov 2005 18:16:04 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Has anyone written an open source viewer for Trimet
	schedules?
Message-ID: <20051104021604.GA27068@gate.kl-ic.com>


I plan to use the bus this weekend, and saw that Trimet has data
files for a proprietary PDA viewer.  Of course, you have to get
past a click-Agree-no-reverse-engineering EULA to get at the
data files, which are at:

http://www.secondkiss.com/trimet/download/palm_os/TriMet.zip
       (for palm .pdb files)

and

http://www.secondkiss.com/trimet/download/windows_mobile/TriMet.zip
       (for windoze CE .sgd files, allegedly using .NET somehow)


Now be good and remember to go to the EULA page first.  It would be
most unfortunate if you somehow found the data files above without
agreeing to the EULA and giving up your rights just so you can access
public information.  Please do not be sneaky and find the appropriate
links by reading the page source rather than clicking Agree...


All that said, it would be handy to read this information with
something besides a PDA.  Are there open source viewers that can
read these files, perhaps translating them into a spreadsheet
format, or front-ending for other processes?  The .pdb format looks
easy to take apart, and the .sgd files are supposedly Compact .NET . 
Seems like just the thing for an ambitious under-employed code
hacker...

Of course, once the tool was ready for demo, we could go straight to
Trimet and ask for this information in binary form, bypassing the
secondkiss website.  In particular, I imagine TriMet can construct
tables for all 60 or so stops on a typical bus line, allowing 
people to build more fine-grained and usable open source apps,
and we could make use of that data.

Keith

of them. They're just different, and they require different skillsets.

I hate not being able to tinker with my computer. At the same time, I 
want my computer to work. I've found that after getting the system 
installed and configured, it stays installed and configured much longer 
with Linux than with Windows.

I have systems at work that get daily use, and have uptimes of more than 
500 days. None of the systems that I manage that have Windows will even 
get close to that length of uptime.

Some would say that distributing a driver where you *can't* compile it 
is evil. I understand that some believe that closed source is a good 
thing, and I'm a "pro choice" type person. You have the choice to close 
your source or not. You have the choice to run Windows, Linux, *BSD, or 
Mac, among others. I don't complain about anyone's choice, until they 
ask me for help with their choice, and I don't agree with it. If they 
want my help, and I know they wouldn't be having the issue if they made 
a different choice, they can either listen to me complain about their 
choice, or make another choice. Either in what OS they use, or in who 
they ask for help. :)

As I said, getting the system installed and configured is a short term 
pain that lasts maybe a day or two, and results in a system that will 
serve for years. Windows may install quicker, but it results in a system 
that will serve for months, maybe a year, and will require much more 
care and vigilance.

Case in point. I don't have to run virus or other scanners on this 
system. None. Nada. The Windows machines on my network run virus 
scanners, spyware scanners, and I configure my mail server to watch for 
things so they won't get through to the windows boxes. If there were no 
Windows boxes, my maintenance on this network would be much less.

From svanhoosen at yahoo.com  Fri Nov  4 09:30:51 2005
From: svanhoosen at yahoo.com (Scott Van Hoosen)
Date: Fri, 4 Nov 2005 09:30:51 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] My Linux switch success story
In-Reply-To: <436AF3E8.3040909@dimstar.net>
Message-ID: <20051104173052.33968.qmail@web51806.mail.yahoo.com>

In light of the recent discussion on difficulties with Linux, I thought
I'd share my linux success story.

I'd been using Windows, and before that OS/2 and DOS, and was never
happy with Microsoft's poorly-designed software. I started using Linux
3 or 4 years ago, Red Hat 7.1 initially, partly because I wanted to try
something different that wouldn't crash constantly, and partly because
I wanted to learn it for work-related skills.

The first couple of weeks were pretty difficult, as things were
unfamiliar from the MS way of doing things, and nobody to hold my hand,
but after a short time I had the basics down. I installed a couple of
games (Quake3 and Return to Castle Wolfenstein), and was happily
surprised at the stability. RtCW in Windows would crash quite often,
maybe once an hour, initiating a 90-second process until I was back at
the desktop again. In Linux, I was able to play through the entire
single-player game without a single crash, which was a miracle compared
to what I was used to.

I've got a Red Hat 9 server that hosts my website, the websites of a
couple of friends and family, our e-mail server, and a file server. It
has run flawlessly, currently with an uptime of 223 days. The last two
times it was shut down were for a hardware change, and when we moved
last December.

I should point out that I have a wife and two sons, and we each have
our own computers. My oldest is more of a computer-geek, so started
using Linux soon after I did, in dual-boot mode so he'd have his games.
My youngest is more into just gaming, so in the past was mostly in
Windows, though his computer was also dual-boot. I wanted my wife to
try Linux, but knew I shouldn't force her. Well, about a year and a
half ago, her power supply died. I had a test machine running Suse all
set up, so I stuck it on her desk, set up Thunderbird for her, showed
her how to launch it, as well as Firefox, and showed her how to install
games through Yast. This "training" took about 10 minutes. Anyway, I
sat back and kept waiting for her to complain, but she didn't. After a
couple weeks, I asked her how she liked Linux, and she responded "It's
fine. Seems the same to me." I fixed her old computer, moved the Linux
drive to it, so she had dual-boot, but she ended up only going to
Windows for a couple of card-making programs. Her hard drive failed a
couple months ago, so I again gave her the spare computer with Linux
already on it. When I mentioned installing Windows again on her second
hard drive, she said to not bother, she never used it anyway.

Recently I did some major changes at home, creating an NIS server which
hosts all our /home folders, as well as a public folder, games folder,
and applications folder. The kids like how they can hop on any
computer, log in, and all their stuff is there: their files, music,
game settings and controls, bookmarks, etc. Also I've been installing
game after game onto the server. It is really nice for me, because I
only have to install the game once, on the network drive, then anyone
can play it. The kids love it too, because now we have a dozen good
games they can play: Quake2, 3 and 4, Doom3, Unreal Tournament 2004,
Neverwinter Nights, Americas Army, Oolite, Return to Castle
Wolfenstein, Cube, Eternal Lands and a couple others. I haven't seen
either kid in Windows for over a week.

The applications folder contains Firefox and Thunderbird, which makes
my job so much easier. I can patch or upgrade it in one place, and then
everyone is running the patched version. Another benefit is it is
painless to try out a different distribution on any workstation,
because all the user's data is saved on the network, as well as major
applications. Also it is easy to back up everyone's data just by
burning the /home partition on the server to a DVD.

There is one drawback I've found with this setup: if the network goes
down, everything goes down. I bought a cheap gigabit switch, which has
crashed on me a couple times during multi-gig file transfers. But as
long as the network is stable, things run really well.

Our servers run Red Hat 9 and Fedora Core 4, and all our workstations
run Suse 9.2, 9.3 and 10. Our firewall is Linux-based IPCop.

I hope this was interesting to someone. :)

-Scott

Yahoo! FareChase: Search multiple travel sites in one click.
http://farechase.yahoo.com

On 11/4/05, Scott Van Hoosen <svanhoosen at yahoo.com> wrote:
> In light of the recent discussion on difficulties with Linux, I thought
> I'd share my linux success story.
>
> I'd been using Windows, and before that OS/2 and DOS, and was never
> happy with Microsoft's poorly-designed software. I started using Linux
> 3 or 4 years ago, Red Hat 7.1 initially, partly because I wanted to try
> something different that wouldn't crash constantly, and partly because
> I wanted to learn it for work-related skills.
>
> The first couple of weeks were pretty difficult, as things were
> unfamiliar from the MS way of doing things, and nobody to hold my hand,
> but after a short time I had the basics down. I installed a couple of
> games (Quake3 and Return to Castle Wolfenstein), and was happily
> surprised at the stability. RtCW in Windows would crash quite often,
> maybe once an hour, initiating a 90-second process until I was back at
> the desktop again. In Linux, I was able to play through the entire
> single-player game without a single crash, which was a miracle compared
> to what I was used to.
>
> I've got a Red Hat 9 server that hosts my website, the websites of a
> couple of friends and family, our e-mail server, and a file server. It
> has run flawlessly, currently with an uptime of 223 days. The last two
> times it was shut down were for a hardware change, and when we moved
> last December.
>
> I should point out that I have a wife and two sons, and we each have
> our own computers. My oldest is more of a computer-geek, so started
> using Linux soon after I did, in dual-boot mode so he'd have his games.
> My youngest is more into just gaming, so in the past was mostly in
> Windows, though his computer was also dual-boot. I wanted my wife to
> try Linux, but knew I shouldn't force her. Well, about a year and a
> half ago, her power supply died. I had a test machine running Suse all
> set up, so I stuck it on her desk, set up Thunderbird for her, showed
> her how to launch it, as well as Firefox, and showed her how to install
> games through Yast. This "training" took about 10 minutes. Anyway, I
> sat back and kept waiting for her to complain, but she didn't. After a
> couple weeks, I asked her how she liked Linux, and she responded "It's
> fine. Seems the same to me." I fixed her old computer, moved the Linux
> drive to it, so she had dual-boot, but she ended up only going to
> Windows for a couple of card-making programs. Her hard drive failed a
> couple months ago, so I again gave her the spare computer with Linux
> already on it. When I mentioned installing Windows again on her second
> hard drive, she said to not bother, she never used it anyway.

out all the cracking attempts.

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Fri Nov  4 12:20:31 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Fri, 4 Nov 2005 12:20:31 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Clipping White Space in PDF File
In-Reply-To: <200511041208.52867.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511041100480.19465@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<200511041208.52867.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511041215590.19465@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Fri, 4 Nov 2005, Eric Wilhelm wrote:

> If you don't mind losing the vector data (assuming that it actually *is*
> vectors), import into the gimp and crop.

Eric,

   Yeah, I do. LaTeX likes .eps, .pst, .pdf, and other vector formats much
better than it does raster formats. The resolution of the latter -- when it's
displaying lines and text projected on a large screen -- really decreases.
Why have typeset slides with poor quality graphics?

> I'm not immediately aware of any open-source vector editors that support
> pdf import.

   I generated the figure with ipe, an open source vector editor. However, my
choice of "page" sizes are A4, A4R (it's written by Europeans), Letter,
800x600, 1024x768, and 1280x1024. That's great if the drawing fills an entire
page. Mine don't.

   As it turns out, while the figure float in LyX looks huge, the figures
display nicely in two-column arrangement on a slide.

Thanks,

Rich

Good afternoon.

I have about 500 domain files that need modifications (changing the mail
server). So I need to change the serial number at the top of the file
and then, lower, change either the ip address of mail.domain.tld or
change the mx record to mail.standarddomain.tld. I don't have a
preference either way, I think they're about equal in the amount of
change I'll have to do later, so the result will depend on the ease of
scripting, because I'm just not going to hand edit 500 domain files.

I'm probably going to write said script in php, because I have php
installed as a cli, and it'll do the job, and I'm most familiar with it.
But I'd like to do it "right," with either sed or awk ('Right,' in this
case, means to me "more like a real systems administrator).. Perl's an
option of course, but I think sed/awk would be sufficient.

If I recall correctly, sed'll take an input file, and I can match
something like (^SOA ... 200\d+) and change it to the right serial
number. How do I go about writing this sort of sed recipe thing? I'm
thinking ...

for i in $(ls /var/named/db.*)
do
sed something < $i > b && mv b $i
done

Your help is appreciated. ;) Thanks.

YAR (russ)

If you're interested the oldie but goody 'linuxconf' will do it all in a 
scripted manner including updating the serial number.

	( http://www.solucorp.qc.ca/linuxconf/ )

I swept through 600-700, though they were split unevenly, on two systems 
changing all the MX records ( we had added in two spoolers ).  Took 
about 10 minutes on the bigger system once I figured out what I wanted 
and how to do it.

If you're interested I'll dig out the script or command line I used.

Of course there are lots of perl modules to handle DNS records also.

Subject: [PLUG] TCP window, how to adjust?
Message-ID: <63696.207.173.0.68.1131149041.squirrel@207.173.0.68>

How can I see what my size Linux TCP receive window is, when running a CLI
ftp client to a get a file from a server?

Am troubleshooting some throughput questions and want to adjust my TCP
window, or at least see what my Linux machine is using &/or negotiating on
a per-download basis.  Hopefully I can adjust the window manually for
testing.  Note these are all client sessions, not worried about using the
machine as a server.

More specifically am trying to find a formula or algorithm that will
predict download throughput with a given bandwidth, TCP window, and
measurable latency.

Thanks!

Steven Raymond wrote:
> More specifically am trying to find a formula or algorithm that will
> predict download throughput with a given bandwidth, TCP window, and
> measurable latency.

Does the window size have *any* effect on throughput assuming it is
large enough to be sane (as is the default)?  Unless you're dealing with
a long fat pipe or something, I suppose... been there, done that.  :-)

I think tcp_wmem (in /proc/sys/net/ipv4) might be what you want to
adjust to change the window size... but I'm not entirely sure there.
Google probably knows for sure.

From eli.stair at gmail.com  Fri Nov  4 16:31:19 2005
From: eli.stair at gmail.com (Eli Stair)
Date: Fri, 4 Nov 2005 16:31:19 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] TCP window, how to adjust?
In-Reply-To: <63696.207.173.0.68.1131149041.squirrel@207.173.0.68>
References: <63696.207.173.0.68.1131149041.squirrel@207.173.0.68>
Message-ID: <f4468cae0511041631p1bcdb21drf4331d7a436aa0ec@mail.gmail.com>

In theory, if you set your TCP window size (or udp application handles
it properly) based on the BDP of pipe/rtt you should achieve as close
to possible of %100 of the (usable) bandwidth.  Basically, if you're
local you don't have to worry (unless you have thousands of clients
causing contention).  If you're running over long distance/latent
connection and you're not getting ~%95 of your bandwidth (presuming
you don't have a biased outbound flow clobbering ACK's), look up "BDP
tcp tuning" and for more info check the Web100.org

Cheers,

/eli

Russ Johnson wrote:

> Another nice thing you'll like with this setup. If their computer dies, 
> when you build them a new one, they log into their desktop and viola! 
> all their stuff is still there. :)

And, don't forget SAMBA. If you have to support Winders machines you can 
still achieve much of the above when the Win machine dies. You'll still 
have to re-install all the Win software and set it up again, but if your 
users store their files on a SAMBA server, they'll still be there. I'm 
stuck with a number of Win98 machines in the house, and my primary one 
died this year. Since I've been kept my data on a SAMBA server, I was 
able to simply (well, I know that's not really accurate!) install and 
set up a "new" Win98 machine and keep working without having to try to 
salvage data from a dead machine.

On Fri, 2005-11-04 at 09:30 -0800, Scott Van Hoosen wrote:
> In light of the recent discussion on difficulties with Linux, I thought
> I'd share my linux success story.
> 
> I'd been using Windows, and before that OS/2 and DOS, and was never
> happy with Microsoft's poorly-designed software. I started using Linux
> 3 or 4 years ago, Red Hat 7.1 initially, partly because I wanted to try
> something different that wouldn't crash constantly, and partly because
> I wanted to learn it for work-related skills.
> 
> The first couple of weeks were pretty difficult, as things were
> unfamiliar from the MS way of doing things, and nobody to hold my hand,
> but after a short time I had the basics down. I installed a couple of
> games (Quake3 and Return to Castle Wolfenstein), and was happily
> surprised at the stability. RtCW in Windows would crash quite often,
> maybe once an hour, initiating a 90-second process until I was back at
> the desktop again. In Linux, I was able to play through the entire
> single-player game without a single crash, which was a miracle compared
> to what I was used to.
> 
> I've got a Red Hat 9 server that hosts my website, the websites of a
> couple of friends and family, our e-mail server, and a file server. It
> has run flawlessly, currently with an uptime of 223 days. The last two
> times it was shut down were for a hardware change, and when we moved
> last December.
> 
> I should point out that I have a wife and two sons, and we each have
> our own computers. My oldest is more of a computer-geek, so started
> using Linux soon after I did, in dual-boot mode so he'd have his games.
> My youngest is more into just gaming, so in the past was mostly in
> Windows, though his computer was also dual-boot. I wanted my wife to
> try Linux, but knew I shouldn't force her. Well, about a year and a
> half ago, her power supply died. I had a test machine running Suse all
> set up, so I stuck it on her desk, set up Thunderbird for her, showed
> her how to launch it, as well as Firefox, and showed her how to install
> games through Yast. This "training" took about 10 minutes. Anyway, I
> sat back and kept waiting for her to complain, but she didn't. After a
> couple weeks, I asked her how she liked Linux, and she responded "It's
> fine. Seems the same to me." I fixed her old computer, moved the Linux
> drive to it, so she had dual-boot, but she ended up only going to
> Windows for a couple of card-making programs. Her hard drive failed a
> couple months ago, so I again gave her the spare computer with Linux
> already on it. When I mentioned installing Windows again on her second
> hard drive, she said to not bother, she never used it anyway.
> 
> Recently I did some major changes at home, creating an NIS server which
> hosts all our /home folders, as well as a public folder, games folder,
> and applications folder. The kids like how they can hop on any
> computer, log in, and all their stuff is there: their files, music,
> game settings and controls, bookmarks, etc. Also I've been installing
> game after game onto the server. It is really nice for me, because I
> only have to install the game once, on the network drive, then anyone
> can play it. The kids love it too, because now we have a dozen good
> games they can play: Quake2, 3 and 4, Doom3, Unreal Tournament 2004,
> Neverwinter Nights, Americas Army, Oolite, Return to Castle
> Wolfenstein, Cube, Eternal Lands and a couple others. I haven't seen
> either kid in Windows for over a week.
> 
> The applications folder contains Firefox and Thunderbird, which makes
> my job so much easier. I can patch or upgrade it in one place, and then
> everyone is running the patched version. Another benefit is it is
> painless to try out a different distribution on any workstation,
> because all the user's data is saved on the network, as well as major
> applications. Also it is easy to back up everyone's data just by
> burning the /home partition on the server to a DVD.
> 
> There is one drawback I've found with this setup: if the network goes
> down, everything goes down. I bought a cheap gigabit switch, which has
> crashed on me a couple times during multi-gig file transfers. But as
> long as the network is stable, things run really well.
> 
> Our servers run Red Hat 9 and Fedora Core 4, and all our workstations
> run Suse 9.2, 9.3 and 10. Our firewall is Linux-based IPCop.
> 
> I hope this was interesting to someone. :)
> 
> -Scott

From nsxfreddy at gmail.com  Fri Nov  4 23:02:43 2005
From: nsxfreddy at gmail.com (Jason R. Martin)
Date: Fri, 4 Nov 2005 23:02:43 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] TCP window, how to adjust?
In-Reply-To: <63696.207.173.0.68.1131149041.squirrel@207.173.0.68>
References: <63696.207.173.0.68.1131149041.squirrel@207.173.0.68>
Message-ID: <c29537840511042302w14dc7a02k79e4eb225ae6ecc@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/4/05, Steven Raymond <stever at woo-hoo.com> wrote:
> How can I see what my size Linux TCP receive window is, when running a CLI
> ftp client to a get a file from a server?

Well you could run tcpdump, for example:

jrmartin at matchbox:~$ sudo tcpdump port ftp
tcpdump: verbose output suppressed, use -v or -vv for full protocol decode
listening on eth0, link-type EN10MB (Ethernet), capture size 96 bytes
16:57:14.007608 IP matchbox.martins.36874 > zeus-pub1.kernel.org.ftp:
S 66568643:66568643(0) win 5840 <mss 1460,sackOK,timestamp 8118980
0,nop,wscale 2>
16:57:14.042245 IP zeus-pub1.kernel.org.ftp > matchbox.martins.36874:
S 761033470:761033470(0) ack 66568644 win 5792 <mss
1460,sackOK,timestamp 3329092979 8118980,nop,wscale 2>

Notice the "win 5840" and "win 5792", the advertised windows for my
system and kernel.org respectively.

But I doubt that those are what you care about, since they are dynamic
and change depending on how many outstanding packets haven't been
processed.  You probably want the send and receive buffer sizes,
SO_SNDBUF and SO_RCVBUF, set by the application.  I don't see a way to
set them for my ftp client, but you can change the system-wide
defaults in /proc/sys/net/ipv4/tcp_wmem and
/proc/sys/net/ipv4/tcp_rmem.

> Am troubleshooting some throughput questions and want to adjust my TCP
> window, or at least see what my Linux machine is using &/or negotiating on
> a per-download basis.  Hopefully I can adjust the window manually for
> testing.  Note these are all client sessions, not worried about using the
> machine as a server.
>
> More specifically am trying to find a formula or algorithm that will
> predict download throughput with a given bandwidth, TCP window, and
> measurable latency.

The bandwidth-delay product is what you're looking for.  Basically if
your window is smaller than the bandwidth * delay then you will not
keep the pipe full.  This might help you:

http://www.speedguide.net/bdp.php

Jason


From david.fleck at mchsi.com  Sat Nov  5 05:52:34 2005
From: david.fleck at mchsi.com (David Fleck)
Date: Sat, 5 Nov 2005 07:52:34 -0600 (CST)
Subject: [PLUG] awk and sed vs php
In-Reply-To: <1131139021.7676.8.camel@badger.had1.or.comcast.net.>
References: <1131139021.7676.8.camel@badger.had1.or.comcast.net.>
Message-ID: <20051105074813.C10197@grond.sourballs.org>

On Fri, 4 Nov 2005, Russ Gilman-Hunt wrote:
> If I recall correctly, sed'll take an input file, and I can match
> something like (^SOA ... 200\d+) and change it to the right serial
> number. How do I go about writing this sort of sed recipe thing? I'm
> thinking ...
>
> for i in $(ls /var/named/db.*)
> do
> sed something < $i > b && mv b $i
> done
>

Pretty much.  In general, it would look like

sed -e 's/regex_for_old_string/new_string/' $i > tmp && mv tmp $i


or, if you wanted to apply the transform to certain lines, rather than 
every line, you can pass in a regex to match those lines:

sed -e '/line_regex/s/regex_for_old_string/new_string/' $i > tmp && mv tmp $i



--
David Fleck
david.fleck at mchsi.com

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Sat Nov  5 06:18:30 2005

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Sat Nov  5 08:58:09 2005
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)
Date: Sat, 05 Nov 2005 08:58:09 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] simple plotting question for 'R'
In-Reply-To: <20051105075738.V10197@grond.sourballs.org>
References: <20051105075738.V10197@grond.sourballs.org>
Message-ID: <436CE4A1.9040109@cesmail.net>

The y-axis is normally at zero on a plot. If R is giving you something 
else, try this:

 > plot(x, y, pch=".", ylim=c(0, max(y))

The 'pch="."' piece makes the points small dots rather than the default 
circles. If you like the default circles (I don't) just leave that out. 
And if you have a better upper limit than the maximum of y, substitute 
that as the second argument of the 'c' function call.

I've been using R for about five years; please feel free to pick my 
brain off list or on list.

One other tip ... type

 > help.start()

That will bring up an HTML help page with links to all the manuals, 
links to all the packages you have installed, and a search engine!

David Fleck wrote:

> I'm trying to learn to use the statistics package R 
> (http://www.r-project.org/).  I want to produce a simple scatterplot

On Sat, 2005-11-05 at 07:52 -0600, David Fleck wrote:
> Pretty much.  In general, it would look like
> 
> sed -e 's/regex_for_old_string/new_string/' $i > tmp && mv tmp $i
> 
> 
> or, if you wanted to apply the transform to certain lines, rather than 
> every line, you can pass in a regex to match those lines:
> 
> sed -e '/line_regex/s/regex_for_old_string/new_string/' $i > tmp && mv tmp $i

Beautiful. Thank you.

From aschlemm at comcast.net  Sat Nov  5 15:52:07 2005
From: aschlemm at comcast.net (Tony Schlemmer)
Date: Sat, 5 Nov 2005 15:52:07 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Tuning Netgear VFS-318
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511050614570.23025@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511050614570.23025@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <200511051552.07307.aschlemm@comcast.net>

On Saturday 05 November 2005 06:18, Rich Shepard wrote:
>    I'm using a Netgear VFS-318 not only as the firewall but also as the
> switch for the internal network. I've realized that the internal data
> transfer rates are terribly slow: less than 100 Kb/sec, not the several
> Mb/sec I used to see with the LinkSys switches. Despite my looking at the
> admin pages, I cannot find anything mis-configured that would explain these
> slow speeds.
>
>    Some of you use this appliance, and I'm hoping you might have some
> insight to share with me on how to improve the intranet data transfer
> speeds.
>
> Thanks,
>
> Rich

The FVS318 doesn't have much in the way of any fancy features. I would check 
what the MTU setting is for the LAN. I have mine set to "default" and the 
transfers are pretty decent between other systems on my network. I have my 
cable modem connected to my FVS318 and it is the central switch in my home 
LAN. I do lots of large file transfers from my laptop to my workstation and 
my laptop is on 802.11g and I get several megabits per second on my large 
"scp" copies.

I've also used the same router in a small office with desktops and servers all 
connected to an FVS318 and there weren't any complains about internal network 
speed. We have a fractional T1 running into the office and so people 
complained about slow downloads from outside the office.

I've got a version 1 of the FVS318 hardware and it's running version 2.4 of 
the Netgear firmware. They've since upgraded the hardware and in newer 
versions they support HTTPS for the web administration page.

Tony

-- 
Anthony Schlemmer
aschlemm at comcast.net

Rich -

Can you check the interface statistics on one of your systems to see
if you are getting any Ethernet errors?  Meaning run traffic for a
while and then check ifconfig and ethtool -S.  Perhaps your system or
the switch are causing errors.  You could also try a different
cable(s).

Do you have another small switch you could try temporarily to verify
it is the router?

Jason

From nsxfreddy at gmail.com  Mon Nov  7 10:55:06 2005
From: nsxfreddy at gmail.com (Jason R. Martin)
Date: Mon, 7 Nov 2005 10:55:06 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] nic-3c59x
In-Reply-To: <1131387955.20903.59.camel@localhost.localdomain>
References: <1131387955.20903.59.camel@localhost.localdomain>
Message-ID: <c29537840511071055u20703df7jc2a71a7dd5119b4d@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/7/05, Vram <lamsokvr at xprt.net> wrote:
> HI
>
> I am running    2.6.12-9-k7-smp
>
>
>
> My NIC card is 3c59x Vortex
>
> The kernel will not load it...
>
> Modules that try to load. are
>
> 3c59x not used
>
> mii.  which is used by 3c59x...  <which is not used>
>
> I can't do an insmod 3c59x..Complains.. No such device..
>
> The problem is.. for some reason the card has no MAC address..
>
> Earlier kernels just complained
>
> loaded the driver and didn't come up
>
> I could change the MAC address, by hand  and
> then bring the card up..
>
>
> This kernel will not let me do that...
>
> How do I get around this??

What does lspci show for the PCI ID for the 3Com?  I have a 3Com NIC
that doesn't have a MAC address either, and the same card also comes
up with a PCI ID of 0xffff:

0000:00:13.0 Ethernet controller: 3Com Corporation 3c905 100BaseTX [Boomerang]
0000:00:14.0 Ethernet controller: 3Com Corporation: Unknown device ffff (rev 78)

Notice the top one is working fine (lspci -n shows the PCI ID for that
one is 0x9050).  If that's the case for you the 3c59x driver won't
recognize the device without hacking the driver source to "recognize"
0xffff as one of the devices it supports.  To do that you need to know
EXACTLY what the card is, to make sure the driver uses the right
features.  My two cards aren't the same, so it took a while to figure
out what the bottom one is supposed to be.

I'd bet the flash that stores the MAC address and such is fried.  If
it's for anything production you'd probably better buy a new card :-(

Jason

Jason,

   I went spelunking in one of the storage boxes in the garage and came up
with a LinkSys 4-port switch. I put two workstations and a notebook on that
switch, then connected it to the Netgear multi-box.

   Re-copying a bunch of security upgrades from the main workstation/server to
the other workstation reached speeds of 1.7MB/s, up from the 46KB/s of the
Netgear alone. So, it must be the FVS318.

   Fortunately, the Netgear is under warranty until July 2009. Unfortunately,
this is the second defective FVS318 in succession. The first one worked fine
as an internal switch, but would not connect to the DSL bridge. When my http
download speeds are double the internal file copies it's not a Good Thing.

I was having a very similar problem and was certain it was one of my many 
cobbled switches.

Turned out, I had a bad NIC in one of my machines that was somehow 
degrading the performance across the board.

The problem went unnoticed on low bandwidth applications, but caused 
massive problems when the bandwidth went up.  There was some discussion of 
the problem here.  I solved it with a $15 NIC.

Well I've never owned a Netgear (at least not since the days of 10Mbps
hubs), nor do I even know what your model is capable of, but I'm still
impressed by my good ol' trusty Linksys WRT54G.  Wired connections for
me, wireless for my wife's laptop (and mine on rare occasions), and
with the Sveasoft firmware I get QoS, statically configured DHCP tied
by MAC address, DNS caching, and even a local DNS domain, all
controlled through a web interface that is almost as intuative as the
original Linksys interface.  If I was more ambitious I could run Snort
on it.  Definitely worth the $50-70 or whatever it costs these days.

Jason "in case you're shopping for a new router" Martin


From keithl at kl-ic.com  Mon Nov  7 13:59:32 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Mon, 7 Nov 2005 13:59:32 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] reducing apache memory usage
Message-ID: <20051107215932.GA10818@gate.kl-ic.com>


I am currently running my Apache server on a virtual host at Vcolo.com,
on a UML with 64MB of memory and 128MB of swap.  Lately, the system has
been running out of memory during nightly backups, which brings down
postfix and sometimes the VPN connection.  I am getting so many
hundreds of spam attempts per minute (most of which are killed before
processing, but...) that postfix can be quite a resource hog .  
I modified the backup control script so that postfix is shut down
during the backups and restarted after (with a later restart in
the crontab in case the backups wedge).


However, Apache is also a memory hog (20 4MB child processes!!!).  I
run 7 low-usage websites on that server, but do not get too many hits
per minute - usually spiders.  I doubt I need that many child processes.
I do use viewcvs and subversion and wiki and https and a bunch of 
other enhancements running, so I can't turn off many of the modules.

To keep Apache in bounds, I went into /etc/httpd/conf/httpd.conf and
reduced some of the settings:

...
<IfModule prefork.c>
# StartServers       8
# MinSpareServers    5
# MaxSpareServers   20
# MaxClients       150
# MaxRequestsPerChild  1000
StartServers       2             
MinSpareServers    2
MaxSpareServers    3
MaxClients        15
MaxRequestsPerChild  100
</IfModule>
...

Does this look reasonable?  The sites still seem quite responsive.
Are there better ways to slim down Apache?

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs


From bsr at spek.org  Mon Nov  7 14:20:58 2005
From: bsr at spek.org (Brent Rieck)
Date: Mon, 07 Nov 2005 14:20:58 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] reducing apache memory usage
In-Reply-To: <20051107215932.GA10818@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20051107215932.GA10818@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <436FD34A.9080502@spek.org>

Keith Lofstrom wrote:
...
> MaxRequestsPerChild  100
...
> Does this look reasonable?

I can't speak to slimming apache down but I would consider increasing 
MaxRequestsPerChild to its former value as it controls the number of 
requests each child handles until it gets killed and a new one started. 
  Unless you have a memory leak a value of 1000 is reasonable, though if 
you have a memory leak setting MaxRequestsPerChild to a low number is 
treating the symptom not the problem, but you probably knew that.

There are a few httpds (thttpd, lighttpd, others probably) that are 
smaller than apache and may fit your needs.

--Brent

From gilmanhunt at comcast.net  Tue Nov  8 13:12:14 2005
From: gilmanhunt at comcast.net (Russ Gilman-Hunt)
Date: Tue, 08 Nov 2005 13:12:14 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] mysqlBind project?
Message-ID: <1131484335.8387.10.camel@badger.had1.or.comcast.net.>

One of the weak points in this application my new 'work' ( for lack of a
better word ) is how it handles named. Basically, the application is a
dynamic domain purchase and hosting provisioning thing. With every
purchase of a domain, this thing rewrites the /etc/named.conf file and
writes a new master file for the named demon, then restarts named.

You can imagine my worries if this thing ever gets the traffic they
would like to see.

But aside from those worries, it's kind of messy. For one thing, there's
a flaw somewhere in it (I think directly in a perl module) that causes
the named files to be written missing a space (for which I have to go in
and fix them): like ...(ipaddress)"IN ...

Eons ago, when I was still young, I recall something about hearings
someone make Bind work with Mysql; if I could have named take the
entries right out of the database, I would have one less point of
failure. And it might be easier to make sweeping changes like "change
all of these mail servers to this ip address."

Has anyone worked with the MysqlBind project from openISP* ? Anyone have
any other resources? 

Yer help, as always, is appreciated.
-YAR

*Link:http://openisp.net/mysqlBind/

The 3c59x is not the same as 3c905 card.  Sure you using the right driver?

>>> lamsokvr at xprt.net 11/07/05 11:19 AM >>>
On Mon, 2005-11-07 at 10:55 -0800, Jason R. Martin wrote:
> On 11/7/05, Vram <lamsokvr at xprt.net> wrote:
> > HI
> >
> > I am running    2.6.12-9-k7-smp
> >
> >
> >
> > My NIC card is 3c59x Vortex
> >
> > The kernel will not load it...
> >
> > Modules that try to load. are
> >
> > 3c59x not used
> >
> > mii.  which is used by 3c59x...  <which is not used>
> >
> > I can't do an insmod 3c59x..Complains.. No such device..
> >
> > The problem is.. for some reason the card has no MAC address..
> >
> > Earlier kernels just complained
> >
> > loaded the driver and didn't come up
> >
> > I could change the MAC address, by hand  and
> > then bring the card up..
> >
> >
> > This kernel will not let me do that...
> >
> > How do I get around this??
> 
> What does lspci show for the PCI ID for the 3Com?  I have a 3Com NIC
> that doesn't have a MAC address either, and the same card also comes
> up with a PCI ID of 0xffff:
> 
> 0000:00:13.0 Ethernet controller: 3Com Corporation 3c905 100BaseTX [Boomerang]
> 0000:00:14.0 Ethernet controller: 3Com Corporation: Unknown device ffff (rev 78)
> 
> Notice the top one is working fine (lspci -n shows the PCI ID for that
> one is 0x9050).  If that's the case for you the 3c59x driver won't
> recognize the device without hacking the driver source to "recognize"
> 0xffff as one of the devices it supports.  To do that you need to know
> EXACTLY what the card is, to make sure the driver uses the right
> features.  My two cards aren't the same, so it took a while to figure
> out what the bottom one is supposed to be.
> 
> I'd bet the flash that stores the MAC address and such is fried.  If
> it's for anything production you'd probably better buy a new card :-(
> 
> Jason




This is what I get..


0000:02:05.0 Ethernet controller: 3Com Corporation 3c905C-TX/TX-M
[Tornado] (rev 78)


Vram

From riznob at gmail.com  Tue Nov  8 15:30:31 2005
From: riznob at gmail.com (Robert Anderson)
Date: Tue, 8 Nov 2005 15:30:31 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] reducing apache memory usage
In-Reply-To: <436FD34A.9080502@spek.org>
References: <20051107215932.GA10818@gate.kl-ic.com> <436FD34A.9080502@spek.org>
Message-ID: <7cbc132f0511081530s4ae60e03i7a35c35bd20cb842@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/7/05, Brent Rieck <bsr at spek.org> wrote:
>
> Keith Lofstrom wrote:
> ...
> > MaxRequestsPerChild 100
> ...
> > Does this look reasonable?
>
> I can't speak to slimming apache down but I would consider increasing
> MaxRequestsPerChild to its former value as it controls the number of
> requests each child handles until it gets killed and a new one started.
> Unless you have a memory leak a value of 1000 is reasonable, though if
> you have a memory leak setting MaxRequestsPerChild to a low number is
> treating the symptom not the problem, but you probably knew that.
>
> There are a few httpds (thttpd, lighttpd, others probably) that are
> smaller than apache and may fit your needs.
>
> --Brent
>
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
>

You may be able to reduce the size of each apache process by not loading
modules that you are not using.

Rob Anderson
riznob at gmail.com

From nsxfreddy at gmail.com  Tue Nov  8 16:00:44 2005
From: nsxfreddy at gmail.com (Jason R. Martin)
Date: Tue, 8 Nov 2005 16:00:44 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] nic-3c59x
In-Reply-To: <s370b112.064@mail.assuredtechsolutions.com>
References: <s370b112.064@mail.assuredtechsolutions.com>
Message-ID: <c29537840511081600w7c72da5br63d4fed660a750f6@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/8/05, Ken Kirkham <kkirkham at assuredtechsolutions.com> wrote:
> The 3c59x is not the same as 3c905 card.  Sure you using the right driver?

The 3c59x driver covers all the "Vortex" and "Boomerang" NICs,
including some 3c9xx cards.  The name is slightly misleading :-)  The
comments at the top of the driver code describe which NICs it
supports, e.g:

http://lxr.linux.no/source/drivers/net/3c59x.c

Jason


From aaron at bavariati.org  Tue Nov  8 19:29:17 2005
From: aaron at bavariati.org (Aaron Burt)
Date: Tue, 8 Nov 2005 19:29:17 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] mysqlBind project?
In-Reply-To: <1131484335.8387.10.camel@badger.had1.or.comcast.net.>
References: <1131484335.8387.10.camel@badger.had1.or.comcast.net.>
Message-ID: <20051109032917.GD14255@bavariati.org>

On Tue, Nov 08, 2005 at 01:12:14PM -0800, Russ Gilman-Hunt wrote:
> One of the weak points in this application my new 'work' ( for lack of a
> better word ) is how it handles named. Basically, the application is a
> dynamic domain purchase and hosting provisioning thing. With every
> purchase of a domain, this thing rewrites the /etc/named.conf file and
> writes a new master file for the named demon, then restarts named.

I've been using BIND-DLZ with Postgres a bit.  It works OK.  Just
remember to index your DNS tables or the loadavg will be pretty high.

http://bind-dlz.sourceforge.net/

Basically, it patches BIND so it can use any number of different
backends.  It hits the backend store every time, so you can
dynamically update DNS entries.

Message-ID: <4372272C.1000108@axpr.net>

Rich Shepard wrote:
>   Has anyone else encountered this inability to reach httpd servers? Is
> there
> anything I can do from here to resolve the issue? Obviously, mail and other
> 'Net services work just fine.

If you've narrowed the problem down to an inability to resolve domain
names, I would start figuring out what link in your DNS chain is down.
The possible culprits include your local configuration on your computer,
any local DNS services (like the local "dnscache"), and your ISP's DNS
servers.

What happens when you skip dnscache?

What happens if you try a different set of DNS servers?

What to DNS tools such as "dig" tell you about your ability to resolve
things at various levels?

Rob

Rich wrote:
>    Locally, dnscache is running. Can I assume, therefore, that the
> problem is with Aracnet's DNS servers?

As I understand it, dnscache doesn't consult other recursive DNS 
servers- queries are resolved from the root servers.  The ISP's servers 
shouldn't affect the behavior of dnscache.  If you can perform lookups 
on outside DNS servers with dig, then perhaps dnscache is wedged.

>    Again, this is something that happened three times in the past.
> Twice were early Sunday mornings two weeks in a row, once was my
> floppyfw having failed, and now today. The access always comes back
> up, but I'm just curious what causes this sporatic outage.

I've found that dnscache will not respond to requests if there is no 
disk space left on the log partition.  I run dnscache on my diskless 
firewall, and sometimes a heavy week of usage will fill /var/log before 
log rotation clears space.  I think my distribution runs a log rotation 
cron weekly on Sunday mornings...

-jk

On 11/10/05, Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:
>    I have a file of IP addresses, in dotted quad notation. Addresses can have
> 2, 3, or 4 of the quads, and I want to convert each address to CIDR. For
> example, if I have 123.456 I'd like to convert that to 123.256.0.0/16; if
> it's 123.456.789, then I'd like to convert that to 123.456.789.0/24.
>

> Rich

> --
> Richard B. Shepard, Ph.D.               |   Author of "Quantifying Environmental
> Applied Ecosystem Services, Inc. (TM)   |  Impact Assessments Using Fuzzy Logic"
> <http://www.appl-ecosys.com>     Voice: 503-667-4517         Fax: 503-667-8863
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
>
Rich,

Just a couple of quick thoughts:
Remember that the CIDR notation isn't nailed to the dotted quad format
so just getting the quads won't do it.  It's either going to take a
heck of an if statement or you might want to convert the dotted quad
to a 32 bit number, then convert that to binary, then convert THAT to
a string.  Then count zeros from the right.  For that kind of
crunching I'd rather use python or even (if forced) perl.  Certainly a
shell script could do it.  I'd just rather have the flexibility of a
full scripting language.

I don't know how you got the data but remember that addess 123.456.789
might be from domain 123.456.  Therefore the CIDR would be 123.456/16,
not 123.456.789/24.

On Thu, Nov 10, 2005 at 10:49:16AM -0800, Rich Shepard wrote:
> I have a file of IP addresses, in dotted quad notation. Addresses
> can have 2, 3, or 4 of the quads, and I want to convert each address
> to CIDR. For example, if I have 123.456 I'd like to convert that to
> 123.256.0.0/16; if it's 123.456.789, then I'd like to convert that
> to 123.456.789.0/24.

> would be the simplest. Am I better off searching for each group
> separately (e.g., all /16 separate from all /24 and all /32)? 

I think so.  This looks like a one-off, so just do a clever
search-and-replace in vi or something.  If you want to repeat it,
port your vi searches to sed.

Since this is, as you mentioned, a spam-blocking application, you may
want to a) throw out all but the /32s; b) consider using one of the
fine DNSBL services that do all this work for you for free; c) use
the very cool temporary-blocklist firewall technique Randal Schwarz
described at a recent AT.



From mikeraz at patch.com  Thu Nov 10 12:35:10 2005

Aaron Burt wrote:
> Since this is, as you mentioned, a spam-blocking application, you may
> want to a) throw out all but the /32s; b) consider using one of the
> fine DNSBL services that do all this work for you for free; c) use
> the very cool temporary-blocklist firewall technique Randal Schwarz
> described at a recent AT.

Options a) and c) will not do much against spam sent to his personal email
account (without accompanying other, invalid addresses) so we should add
in d) deploy dspam, bogofilter or other intelligent spam learning ware.

> Rich,
> 
> Just a couple of quick thoughts:
> Remember that the CIDR notation isn't nailed to the dotted quad format
> so just getting the quads won't do it.  It's either going to take a
> heck of an if statement or you might want to convert the dotted quad
> to a 32 bit number, then convert that to binary, then convert THAT to
> a string.  Then count zeros from the right.  For that kind of
> crunching I'd rather use python or even (if forced) perl.  Certainly a
> shell script could do it.  I'd just rather have the flexibility of a
> full scripting language.
> 
> I don't know how you got the data but remember that addess 123.456.789
> might be from domain 123.456.  Therefore the CIDR would be 123.456/16,
> not 123.456.789/24.




Someone correct if I am wrong

But, classful    Class A is   0 to 127  With 0 and 127 abstaining.

Therefore with classful  notation you could say 123.456.789.0/8

But, given 123.456.789.0

I have NO idea what is happening till you give me THE MASK..



My story and I am sticking with it...

Hi Vram,

This is what I use:

echo "Enabling forwarding ..."
echo 1 > /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_forward

Marc

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Fri Nov 11 15:31:22 2005
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Fri, 11 Nov 2005 15:31:22 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Installing perl libraries -- question
In-Reply-To: <BAY108-F4CBA7EE1E3AAB15358CC9B8590@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY108-F4CBA7EE1E3AAB15358CC9B8590@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <200511111531.23038.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from Vincent Yau
# on Friday 11 November 2005 02:15 pm:

>ncftp://ftp.perl.org/pub/CPAN/MIRRORED.BY./

That's an odd url.  What port does the ncftp:// protocol use?

Your (root's?) ~/.cpan/CPAN/MyConfig.pm should have a 'urllist' array 
reference in the Config = { ... } hash somewhere.

...
  'urllist' => [
         "ftp://archive.progeny.com/CPAN/",
         "http://cpan.develooper.com/",
         "http://www.perl.com/CPAN/",
   ],
...

You can also use the ("o conf urllist push ftp://myurl/") instructions 
that it gives you in the error message, provided that you start the 
shell ("perl -MCPAN -e shell")

If you're on debian (or most distros for that matter) you will find a 
ready-made package for common modules.

--Eric

From merlyn at stonehenge.com  Sat Nov 12 02:35:07 2005
From: merlyn at stonehenge.com (Randal L. Schwartz)
Date: 12 Nov 2005 02:35:07 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: Installing perl libraries -- question
References: <BAY108-F4CBA7EE1E3AAB15358CC9B8590@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <86oe4qnoh0.fsf@blue.stonehenge.com>

>>>>> "Vincent" == Vincent Yau <v_yau3 at hotmail.com> writes:

Vincent> bash-2.05$ perl -MCPAN -e 'install "LWP::Simple"'
Vincent> LWP not available
Vincent> Please check, if the URLs I found in your configuration file
Vincent> (ncftp://ftp.perl.org/pub/CPAN/MIRRORED.BY./) are valid. The urllist can be
Vincent> edited. E.g. with 'o conf urllist push ftp://myurl/'

That's really messed up.  Go into interactive mode:

        perl -MCPAN -e shell

and then reconfigure it with:

        o conf init

and answer all the questions *carefully*, and then:

        o conf commit

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sat Nov 12 07:49:05 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sat, 12 Nov 2005 07:49:05 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] buying Mini-ITX in PDX - Linux compatability
In-Reply-To: <ca5165530511101204o285af821he7ba890ae2c4f669@mail.gmail.com>
References: <20051110185451.GE18975@peak.org>
	<ca5165530511101204o285af821he7ba890ae2c4f669@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20051112154905.GA7003@gate.kl-ic.com>

On 11/10/05, Eric House <fixin at peak.org> wrote:
> I'm looking to build a fanless Linux box, probably based on a Mini-ITX
> board, and want to get the parts in Portland.  Can anybody recommend a
> shop that 1) knows what supports Linux (or can look it up); carries
> Mini-ITX boards, cases, etc; and 3) is open on Saturdays?

On Thu, Nov 10, 2005 at 12:04:25PM -0800, Larry Brigman wrote:
> The only place I have found Mini-ITX boards is at Fry's.  Even then
> the ones they carry have fans.

I recently purchased a Shuttle ST62K from Fry's - it is one of the
older and slower and less expensive miniITX boxes, and it does have
a fan.  However, the fan is pretty quiet.  It fires up relatively
loudly when the machine boots, then slows during normal operation. 
With the case on, the single fan is somewhat quieter than the house's
central air heating duct, which is pretty good for a 2GHz+ Pentium.

You are not likely to find a faster machine without a fan of some
sort.  The ST62K has a heat pipe from the CPU chip to the main fan,
so there are not multiple fans making noise at least.  This machine
will be going into my wife's office, and she likes quiet.

I remember there were issues with drivers - I had to use Fedora core
4 and tweak with the X configuration, older distros did not work.
But maybe that's just me.  I don't have sound working yet - but as
I said, my wife likes quiet.  The ST62K video DAC is a little wussy,
and consequently the pixels are not very sharp, which can lead to Moire
effects on an LCD monitor.  If you find a low power unit with a DVI
connector, or an AGP slot, I would be interested in hearing about it.

Be attentive to chipsets and drivers.  The mini-ITX units use weird
chipsets to reduce power, and there may be driver issues with the
unit you select - sorta like some laptops only worse.   

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

refers to every part of the process that follows the taking of the
picture, through final output and permanent storage. Anyone who shoots,
scans, or stores digital photographs is practicing some form of DAM, but
most of us are not doing so systematically or efficiently. In "The DAM
Book: Digital Asset Management for Photographers," photographer Peter

protect, and re-use photographs, focusing on best practices for digital
photographers using Adobe Photoshop CS2.

designed to deliver what you need to know.
<http://www.oreilly.com/catalog/winxpfstmm/>

Publisher: No Starch Press
ISBN: 159327064X
Just Say No to Microsoft begins by tracing Microsoft's rise from tiny
startup to monopolistic juggernaut and explains how the company's
practices have discouraged innovation, stunted competition, and helped
foster an environment ripe for viruses, bugs and hackers. Readers learn
how they can dump Microsoft products and continue to be productive.

and Mac, and outlines various software applications that can replace the
familiar Microsoft products.

things has become one of the fastest up-and-coming social trends in the
US, and thus has drawn the litigious eye of large entertainment and
media companies. Andy remains optimistic, however, that modders
themselves can find ways to shift the focus away from modding as a legal
issue, and toward a view of modding as a social and business issue.

distributions as well as the specialist distros, and for who (or what)
each distro is best suited.

***JBoss Cache as a POJO Cache

POJO caches work.

From ehem at m5p.com  Sat Nov 12 16:19:32 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Sat, 12 Nov 2005 16:19:32 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] The Saga Continues - was: New To The List
In-Reply-To: <20051112200004.7566E41D6@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200511130019.jAD0JWEU050163@m5p.com>

>From: frank hunt <debidog97124 at yahoo.com>
> First of all, thanks to all of you who gave me advice,
> help and hand-holding last night.  I am still unable
> to boot to my original HDD but I have made a little
> progress.  I mounted that drive to another Linux
> system and I can see most of the files.  Most.  The
> missing filesets are all of the data files from my web
> site (about 8000 html files and associated images). 
> Something nasty must have happened during the aborted
> dd backup process is all I can figure.  Now I'm in
> deep doo-doo.  My latest backup is months old and (of
> course) I have done MAJOR surgery to the site since
> then.  I cannot re-create most of it. 

Hmm, mixed prognosis here. On one hand a `dd` mistake could do massive
damage. On the other hand, the fact that there is enough present to get
you the error message you've seen is hopeful.

So standard recovery methods. Don't do anything that writes to the drive.
Use dd/dd_rescue to copy raw images of the involved filesystems to
another drive. Run `fsck -f` on a copy of the filesystems. This should
hopefully retrieve most of the files (I'm guessing you destroyed
metadata, the files /might/ still be present).

Then you get onto rebuilding. Sounds like your root filesystem is
sufficiently toast that a bare-metal reinstall is really needed. For a
quick fix, your original installation method should work. For long term
I'd think in terms of going for either a recent Fedora or perhaps Debian.
I'd suggest Debian, sounds like you've the experience to take it on, and
over the long-term very little maintenance is needed.

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Sun Nov 13 09:19:03 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Sun, 13 Nov 2005 09:19:03 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] UPS for linux
In-Reply-To: <BAY108-F3FC28E15DE359FDC376FAB85B0@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY108-F3FC28E15DE359FDC376FAB85B0@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511130913590.16710@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Sun, 13 Nov 2005, Vincent Yau wrote:

> Can anyone suggest an UPS  with Linux control software to perform graceful
> shutdown (that you have tried and happy to recommend)?

Vincent,

   Yup. The APC Smart-UPS series. I bought a refurbished 1400VA model along
with the serial cable. I've set up apcupsd on the server (directly connected
to the UPS via cable) and on the other host (as a slave without a direct
connection). The APC hardware is very well designed and made (I had bad
experiences with Tripp-Lite years ago), their linux daemon is very well
documented, and there are several rebuilders that sell refurbished units with
new batteries and a warranty for a very reasonable price. They also will
reboot the system when the power returns ... I think. I'd have to look that
one up again.

   Get plenty of spare capacity. I'm running a total of 700W (maximum) power
supplies on a UPS rated for 1,000W.

Rich

All-
I was hoping someone could provide a brief bonehead-level  primer on setting

returns "localhost" that I should check /etc/hostname or /etc/hosts and my

There are samples of what the /var/qmail/control files should contain, which

2nd level domain examples:
# hostname --fqdn
should return "wh0rd.org"
# cat me
should contain "wh0rd.org"
# cat defaultdomain
should contain "wh0rd.org"
# cat plusdomain
should contain "wh0rd.org"
# cat locals
should contain "wh0rd.org"

should contain "wh0rd.org"

the example for 3rd level domains is a little less confusing:

3rd level domain examples:
# hostname --fqdn
should return "mail.wh0rd.org"
# cat me
should contain "mail.wh0rd.org"
# cat defaultdomain
should contain "wh0rd.org"
# cat plusdomain
should contain "wh0rd.org"
# cat locals
should contain "mail.wh0rd.org"
# cat rcpthosts
should contain "mail.wh0rd.org"


.....Starting here, I will be referring to my real domain name
("towermonky.com") rather than the "wh0rd.org"  from the howto.......

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Sun Nov 13 15:34:58 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Sun, 13 Nov 2005 15:34:58 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] qmail hostname and domain confusion
In-Reply-To: <OMEBINHFEBMFOKIAIEADIEJIDLAA.ble.nordlund@verizon.net>
References: <OMEBINHFEBMFOKIAIEADIEJIDLAA.ble.nordlund@verizon.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511131529410.16710@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Sun, 13 Nov 2005, Brian & Lori Nordlund wrote:

> However, the way I read it there seems to be some blur between the hostname
> of the server and the domain being served. To start, there is a section
> explaining that if
> # hostname --fqdn
> returns "localhost" that I should check /etc/hostname or /etc/hosts and my
> DNS to make sure "everything is correct".  Then once I have "checked" then
> edit the config files in /var/qmail/control.  There is also a reference that
> the file /var/qmail/control/me should contain the hostname.  Now for the
> confusion:

Brian,

   The hostname should be the name of the machine itself, not just
'localhost.' If it's a fully-qualified domain name (FQDN), then it would be
of the form mehost.example.com; localhost.localdomain is a synonym.

> There are samples of what the /var/qmail/control files should contain, which
> is where I get confused.  There are examples to be used if you are doing a
> "2nd level domain" followed by examples for doing a third level domain:

> 2nd level domain examples:
> # hostname --fqdn
> should return "wh0rd.org"
> # cat me
> should contain "wh0rd.org"
> # cat defaultdomain
> should contain "wh0rd.org"
> # cat plusdomain
> should contain "wh0rd.org"
> # cat locals
> should contain "wh0rd.org"
> # cat rcpthosts
> should contain "wh0rd.org"

   Your domain should be your equivalent of example.com. The hostname is the
particular host that holds the mail server (MTA).

> Now tell me if I'm a complete loon, but it looks to me like we are mixing
> the definition of host and domain.  In order to force # hostname --fqdn to
> return "wh0rd.org" wouldn't I be using a domain name for my server?  Maybe
> the example for 3rd level domains is a little less confusing:

   See above; first paragraph.

> .....Starting here, I will be referring to my real domain name
> ("towermonky.com") rather than the "wh0rd.org"  from the howto.......

   Then your domain name is towermonky.com and the FQDN would be
mail.towermonky.com (or the actual name of the machine.)

Rich
