From aschlemm at comcast.net  Sun Nov 13 17:28:19 2005
From: aschlemm at comcast.net (Tony Schlemmer)
Date: Sun, 13 Nov 2005 17:28:19 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] UPS for linux
In-Reply-To: <BAY108-F3FC28E15DE359FDC376FAB85B0@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY108-F3FC28E15DE359FDC376FAB85B0@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <200511131728.19824.aschlemm@comcast.net>

On Saturday 12 November 2005 22:31, Vincent Yau wrote:
> Hi:
>
> I am hoping to get one of those UPS that would not
> only protect against sudden power outage
> but also automatically performs graceful shutdown.
>
> I tried one earlier this year that had a Linux software
> (using SNMP via serial interface to the UPS) but did not
> work very well.  And their tech support was less than helpful.
> I dropped the issue but I need to pick it up
> again since I do really need one that works this time.
>
> Can anyone suggest an UPS  with Linux control software to perform
> graceful shutdown (that you have tried and happy to recommend)?
>
> thanks
>
> --Vincent

I own a number of APC UPS for the many and most of the companies I've done 
work for over the last 10 years have used APC UPS boxes as well. For Linux 
support I like to use "apcupsd" which is monitoring daemon for APC boxes.

It's quite configurable via a configuration file and allows a Linux system to 
be shutdown based on your preferences. You can have it signal your system to 
shutdown based on how long its been running on battery or even better IMHO is 
when the battery level is below a certain point.  I don't know if most 
distros include it precompiled or not but I usually obtain the source code 
and compile it myself. 

"apcupsd" can also be setup in a client/server setup which I find useful in 
cases where I have a large UPS that can support multiple systems. One system 
with the signaling cable monitors the UPS and the other systems are clients 
and receive notifications from the server system. An important point to 
consider when using a network to signal other systems is to ensure that the 
switch the systems are using for their network connection should also be on 
an UPS otherwise signaling will be lost during a power failure.

I've used "apcupsd" with both serial and USB signling cables without any 
issues. Some of the newer APC BackUPS RS-1500 and XS-1500 only support a USB 
signaling cable. I had to specify that I wanted USB support through the 
configuration script that setups up the build environment.

At one time APC had a version of their PowerChute software that ran under 
Linux and I was using that but that was more than 4 years ago and when I 
found myself needing a UPS monitor again sometime later I found "apcupsd". 
There's not fancy GUI or anything but it does the job just for all of the 
systems I've managed over the last few years.

[snip]

-- 
Anthony Schlemmer
aschlemm at comcast.net

If you give your logs a good look, you will most likely find references 
to all kinds of "stuff" in there.  I run a check daily looking for 404 
errors with an associated .exe or .cgi or .pl associated with them.  
These are caused by someone up to no good.  I trap their IP address and 
exclude them from my web site from then on with the Deny <IP> directive.

> graceful shutdown (that you have tried and happy to recommend)?

APC SmartUPS.  FreeGeek sells used, tested ones but you may have to
get your own special serial cable.

For software, I strongly recommend NUT.  http://www.networkupstools.org/

PCs if they're all plugged into the same UPS.  Also there are some
nice monitoring widgets that talk to NUT.

Some vendors supply rails in different lengths. And most rails can
be adjusted +- a few inches.

If just needing a couple inches, use a spacer, but ! you have to be
careful in that you now have to add the bolt/spacer to the loading
calculation. This is a lawyer infested world.

Any decent hardware store will have what you need. In a pinch I've
even used over sized nuts to build up a spacer.

-pete

Quoting Wil Cooley <wcooley at nakedape.cc>:

> On Sun, 2005-11-13 at 06:31 +0000, Vincent Yau wrote:
> 
> > Can anyone suggest an UPS  with Linux control software to perform
> > graceful shutdown (that you have tried and happy to recommend)?
> 
> I recommend Network UPS Tools: http://www.networkupstools.org/ and any
> of the supported UPS brands.  A note WRT APC: the low-end models, in
> addition to being kinda lousy as a UPS, also tend to have USB monitor
> interfaces, which when I checked a few months ago we're not as well
> supported as the serial.
> 
> Wil
> -- 
> Wil Cooley                                 wcooley at nakedape.cc
> Naked Ape Consulting                        http://nakedape.cc
> * * * * Linux, UNIX, Networking and Security Solutions * * * *
> 

If you know what you're doing building surge suppression, ac/dc conversion,
and power boost circuitry, you can make your own.  I have an APC smart UPS
su1000net which works well using nuts, but I need to replace the battery
and it appears that these aren't made anymore.  The other thing you're 
going to want to make if you roll your own ups is a serial ciruit that
will communicate with Linux so that you can do graceful shutdowns.

If someone were smart, they'd start a business making usb UPS'es 
specifically for Linux.  I wish someone would do the same for
multi function all in one printers/scanners/fax/copy machines 
as well.

Find an APC smart ups that signals over a serial line, I found mine on
E-Bay.  Longer term, I hope we don't all have to roll our own.

     Michael C. Robinson

-rw-r--r--  1 vram vram       9 2004-12-17 13:15 jim



Command


vram at Aether:~/tmp $ chmod 1777 jim



After 

-rwxrwxrwt  1 vram vram        9 2004-12-17 13:15 jim



See the T on world/others

Using Windows Explorer on Win98SE, I've just deleted a recent (in other 
words, not backed up) file from a Samba shared directory on an EXT-2 
file system. It's not critical if I can't recover it, but I figured this 
is a good example to learn on.

So far, nothing's been written to that drive since the deletion. I've 
searched "undelete" on the Linux specific part of Google, and have 
started following the instructions at:

http://www.linux.com/howtos/Ext2fs-Undeletion-4.shtml

As the file resides on my 60MB drive, debugfs: lsdel is taking some time.

Is there a better way? The last time I had occasion to do this sort of 
thing was many years ago on a DOS machine where it was a simple matter 
of using some Norton tool and changing the deleted flag on the filename. 
I was hoping for something equally as simple, but I realize that may be 
wishful thinking.

Anyway, any alternative recommendations will be gratefully received.

From david.fetter at fetterconsulting.com  Mon Nov 14 14:12:38 2005
From: david.fetter at fetterconsulting.com (David Fetter)
Date: Mon, 14 Nov 2005 14:12:38 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Undelete with Samba
In-Reply-To: <4379047B.6040403@comcast.net>
References: <4379047B.6040403@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <1132006358.8215.47.camel@thoth.oit.pdx.edu>

Newer versions of samba support some of the windows vfs object
specifications.  I used the following within the smb.conf for a client
to achieve a recyclebin function so that things aren't directly deleted
just as is normal operations under a windows desktop.

        # the options below are what will implement the recycle bin.
        vfs object = recycle
        recycle:repository = /recyclebin/%U
        recycle:touch = Yes
        recycle:keeptree = Yes
        recycle:versions = Yes
        recycle:noversions = *.tmp,*.temp,*.o,*.obj,*.TMP,*.TEMP
        recycle:exclude = *.tmp,*.temp,*.o,*.obj,*.TMP,*.TEMP
        recycle:excludedir = /recyclebin,/tmp,/temp,/TMP,/TEMP



On Mon, 2005-11-14 at 13:41 -0800, Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> Using Windows Explorer on Win98SE, I've just deleted a recent (in other

From ehem at m5p.com  Mon Nov 14 16:04:54 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Mon, 14 Nov 2005 16:04:54 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] strange http requests
In-Reply-To: <20051114161828.6D15344B7@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200511150004.jAF04skO076513@m5p.com>

>From: fh oregon <linux at frankhunt.com>
> If you give your logs a good look, you will most likely find references 
> to all kinds of "stuff" in there.  I run a check daily looking for 404 
> errors with an associated .exe or .cgi or .pl associated with them.  
> These are caused by someone up to no good.  I trap their IP address and 
> exclude them from my web site from then on with the Deny <IP> directive.

Problem is you're most likely to catch worms and zombies this way, than
do any real good. In the case of dialup systems you're going to have to
block large numbers of IP addresses, and you get a lot of uninvolved
parties.

Better is to provide an alert to the poor sap whose machine has been
turned into swiss cheese. In this general category was the classic of
creating a 64KB file of zeros named "default.ida", because this crashed
the worm.

From rvoshell at touchstonetech.com  Mon Nov 14 18:29:09 2005
From: rvoshell at touchstonetech.com (Randy Voshell)
Date: Mon, 14 Nov 2005 18:29:09 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Sticky bits...
Message-ID: <s378d79a.005@mail.touchstonetech.com>

The "1" in 1777 is the sticky bit... so called because of its antiquated
use in causing executable files to "stick" in swap space.  Linux
apparently ignores the sticky bit set on files.

When the sticky bit is set on a (shared) directory, the files within the
directory can only be renamed or deleted by the file owner, the
directory owner, or root.  Obviously, the term "sticky bit" comes from
the older use of the bit.

The execute permission for world is coded as T when the sticky bit is
set, and as t when both the sticky and executable is set.


============
Randy Voshell
http://www.touchstonetech.com
LPIC/MasterCNI/CDE/CLP/CLE/MCSE/MCT

about?

Why doesn't ls -l show all permissions if there are special sticky bits?
Is there a command that will show these bits?

south before.  The previous time a whois turned it up and a few 
days/weeks later it turned up again at a different hosting company. 
There are gory details but I won't bore you with them.

That time I was trying to get in contact with him about some ( paying ) 
work to add and fix functionality in the code.  Even after his domain 
returned I could get no replys to email.

This time I went looking for the online documentation and now the domain 
doesn't even show up in a whois.  ( Much of the site is saved at 
archive.org ).

Enough background.  So I have copies of the files and want to add and 
correct some functionality in the code and possibly release it.  Where 
do I stand legally since it is not OSS?  All he asked is that he be 
recognized as the author and if it was used commercially make a 
"donation" of $5 - $30 per application it is used in ( via. PayPal ).

Semi-gory details.  The code package is fValidate.  The author is Peter 
Bailey.  The domain is peterbailey.net .

Thoughts, ideas, and off list if this is too off topic.


Rod
--

info on the addresses' owners with whois.  Just don't abuse whois--use
it once for each IP range, rather than for each and every address.

	From: Matthews, Joshua D. [mailto:JMatthews at kforce.com] 
	Sent: Tuesday, November 15, 2005 10:39 AM
	To: wamorita at hevanet.com

	Software Development Engineer 1

	Job Description

	We are responsible for assisting the United States Department of
Justice and several State governments in enforcing the Microsoft anti-trust
settlement. Our duties include verifying that Microsoft's software products
behave in a manner consistent with the settlement's consent decree. To that
end, we are currently involved in the prototyping of a large number of
client/server based network protocols as part of a document validation
effort. The server side code is being developed on a RedHat Linux platform
in C++ and will be tested against Microsoft Windows XP clients to insure
proper functionality and interoperability.

	We are looking for Software Development Engineers to work closely
with the prototyping teams Lead Engineers primarily on server side core
development and client side test case generation. Throughout development,
integration and test, a close relationship will be maintained with the Lead
Engineers of the various protocols. The SDE 1 will be responsible for
working under the direction of the Lead, writing C++ code from design
documents provided and augmented with direction from the Lead Engineers
themselves. The SDE 1 will additionally be responsible for writing
functional tests on a Windows XP that will exercise the protocols for
functionality.


	Qualifications

	The ideal candidate will be a creative thinker who is a self-starter
and should be capable of taking ownership of a specified functional area and
delivering results in a robust development environment staffed by some of
the best design engineers in the industry. Candidates should have a strong
Computer Science background and should be fluent in C++ and object oriented
programming. Minimum of 3-5 years work experience and a bachelor's degree in
computer science or related field is required. An advanced degree in
computer science or related field is preferred. Candidates for this position
must have team experience and work well in a team environment.


	Must Have

	*	At least 3 years developing C++ code in a UNIX/Linux and/or
Visual C++ environment. 
	*	Proven experience writing client/server applications on
UNIX/Linux or Win32. 
	*	At least a basic understanding of how to develop RPC
Methods. 
	*	Proven experience writing functional test cases. 

	Prefer to Have

	*	Proven experience writing RPC based client/server
applications. 
	*	Experience developing network applications in a UNIX/Linux
or Win32 environment. 
	*	UNIX/Linux or Windows system level experience, preferably
with protocol stacks. 

	Nice to Have

	*	Experience with streaming media or terminal service
applications. 
	*	Actual work experience writing networking protocols. 
	*	Experience with rights management or client certification. 
	*	Experience writing .NET or web based communications code. 
	*	Experience with security credentials, NTLM, or NetLogon. 

	 

	Individual will be exposed to highly confidential information.
Individual must agree to certain post employment restrictions.
	
	The job is located in Bellevue WA .  No relocation will be paid.  

	Approximate Duration: 1 year

On Tue, Nov 15, 2005 at 08:24:07AM -0800, Roderick A. Anderson wrote:
> 
> The author of some JavaScript code seems to have disappeared off the 
> ... 
> doesn't even show up in a whois.  ( Much of the site is saved at 
> archive.org ).

... including his cell phone number (214-XXX-XXXX Dallas TX area).  
"whois fvalidate.com" lists contact information for him, in Plano
(a suburb NE of Dallas), and an email address on gmail, most 
recently changed in April 2005.  I suggest trying those. 

If THAT comes up empty, you might send an email to the North
Texas Linux User's Group ( ntlug.org ) and ask them if anyone
knows of him and his current status, or of the name of any
Java users groups that cover that portion of Dallas.  


> correct some functionality in the code and possibly release it.  Where 
> do I stand legally since it is not OSS?  All he asked is that he be 
> recognized as the author and if it was used commercially make a 
> "donation" of $5 - $30 per application it is used in ( via. PayPal ).
>
> Semi-gory details.  The code package is fValidate.  The author is Peter 
> Bailey.  The domain is peterbailey.net .

Is there a registered copyright?  Is the source open (that is, readable
and available) but not free?  If Mr Bailey has gone to the Great Coding
Project In The Sky, there might be some issues with releasing the exact
same code on another site, but probably no major problem if you
refactored the code significantly enough, then started a fork under an open
source license.

Or, since he retains copyright and may be commercializing his code, you
may find that the fValidate.com site comes up in a few weeks with an
order form for the code - $99 down, $99 a month for 99 year.  Paranoia...

----

About 1.5 years ago, JW Schultz of (IP address near the Bay Area) died.
It took nearly 6 months to learn the facts of his death, since he was
so very private and secretive that we did not even know his first name. 
However, his dirvish code was open source, so I put it up on a server
and opened it up to development, during the time we were waiting for
more info.  After about a year of public involvement, we have 87 users
on the mailing list and contributions coming in from all over the world,
as well as some pretty significant wins at high profile sites ( OSU
OSL, Berkeley, Cambridge, Dutch Public Television, etc).  
 
That is what open source permits.  If you don't like your own work
or data getting dragged down when another project's leader goes
[ missing | insane | dead ], consider investing your time in something
with an open source license rather than something closed or encumbered. 
There may be enough other users of fValidate in the same pickle that
you can work together to write a replacement, if Mr. Bailey is no
longer able to support you.

Keith

Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

My advice would be to throw away any components of questionable support 
or legality and re-create their functionality from scratch. Software is 
about communication between people and between people and machines. In 
the absence of communication and legally documented rights, what you 
have is a ticking time bomb. Get rid of it *now*!

I thought of you and dirvish as I wondered if something had happened to him.

> About 1.5 years ago, JW Schultz of (IP address near the Bay Area) died.
> It took nearly 6 months to learn the facts of his death, since he was
> so very private and secretive that we did not even know his first name. 
> However, his dirvish code was open source, so I put it up on a server
> and opened it up to development, during the time we were waiting for
> more info.  After about a year of public involvement, we have 87 users
> on the mailing list and contributions coming in from all over the world,
> as well as some pretty significant wins at high profile sites ( OSU
> OSL, Berkeley, Cambridge, Dutch Public Television, etc).  
>  
> That is what open source permits.  If you don't like your own work
> or data getting dragged down when another project's leader goes

tried to get dansguardian working with a k12ltsp server and thin clients.

We would prefer having it all happen on the server without dealing with 
configuring firefox and locking it down for each user.

Lots of searches and reading turned up conflicting information; from 
using ipchains ( verses iptables ) to "it should work out of the box." 
None of them worked.

We, all that were actively working on this, agreed that whiskey wouldn't 
help and aspirin were not as enjoyable ( for the iptables stuff. )  Lots 
of head aches.

Has anyone on the list done this?

There is a server with two NICs -- eth0 connected to a switch and the 
thin clients and eth1 connected to "the Internet".  Since this is going 
into a "shelter" the configuration needs to be simple and robust. ( Did 
I just say Linux? ).


TIA,
Rod

Subject: [PLUG] device and inode number to filename?
Message-ID: <200511171314.54377.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

Hi all,

I'm trying to figure out if there's a way to reach into the depths of a 
filesystem and pull out every filename which is linked to a given inode 
without walking the tree.

I've found some references to an "ncheck" command (that maybe was on 
HPUX?)  So maybe no way to find the source.  It sounded like debugfs -R 
"ncheck <number>" <device> was going to do the trick, but it only 
prints the name of the first file (and continues to do so even when 
only other links (or even no links) remain.)

I realize that it might not be possible to do this in a fs-agnostic way, 
but having never written my own filesystem, I might just need to get 
knocked with a cluestick (e.g. there is no indexed inode table?)  That, 
or maybe someone could tell me the secret code (er, jargon) that 
unlocks the google easter-egg for this level.

Thanks,
Eric

From seniorr at aracnet.com  Thu Nov 17 13:59:25 2005
From: seniorr at aracnet.com (Russell Senior)
Date: 17 Nov 2005 13:59:25 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] device and inode number to filename?
In-Reply-To: <200511171314.54377.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
References: <200511171314.54377.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
Message-ID: <86zmo3q6ki.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "Eric" == Eric Wilhelm <scratchcomputing at gmail.com> writes:

Eric> Hi all, I'm trying to figure out if there's a way to reach into
Eric> the depths of a filesystem and pull out every filename which is
Eric> linked to a given inode without walking the tree.

Not quite sure what you've after, but you can build a mapping from
filename to inode, e.g. using find, but it does involve walking the
tree.  I don't think the filesystem bothers to maintain the reverse
mapping (inode->fname).

  $ find . -inum <n>

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Thu Nov 17 16:09:28 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Thu, 17 Nov 2005 16:09:28 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] A Good Book for TCL/TK
In-Reply-To: <1132271564.21684.0.camel@c-67-171-140-109.hsd1.or.comcast.net>
References: <1132271564.21684.0.camel@c-67-171-140-109.hsd1.or.comcast.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511171606000.1174@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Thu, 17 Nov 2005, Keith wrote:

> Can anyone recommend a good learning for for tcl/tk?

Keith,

   There are a number of books by the author of Tcl/Tk, but why learn that?
Tcl is quite limited as a scripting language compared with python, perl, and
all the rest. Tk is very low level (near Xlib) and does not have the widget
support of GTK+2, wxWidgets, Qt, or even FLTK.

   I started down the Tcl/Tk path about eight years ago and quickly
backtracked for (my then needs) GTK+. Now I'm wrestling with wxPython.

Rich

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Thu Nov 17 20:16:14 2005
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)
Date: Thu, 17 Nov 2005 20:16:14 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] A Good Book for TCL/TK
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511171606000.1174@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <1132271564.21684.0.camel@c-67-171-140-109.hsd1.or.comcast.net>
	<Pine.LNX.4.63.0511171606000.1174@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <437D558E.2010305@cesmail.net>

Yeah ... Tk isn't too bad, but Tcl is a ghastly scripting language. The 
best book I've found so far on Tk is the big O'Reilly one on Perl/Tk. 
Most of the other scripting languages duplicate the Perl interface, so, 
for example, if you want to use Ruby, you'll still want the Perl/Tk book.

The big thing Tk has going for it is that it's ubiquitous, like Perl. 
Instant GUI. But yes, there are much better looking GUI toolkits out 
there. I'm partial to Qt because I'm also partial to KDE, and because 
there's a really good book at Pragmatic Programmers on QT with Ruby. So 
for the near term, that's the way I'm going.

From eharrison at mail.mesd.k12.or.us  Thu Nov 17 21:45:03 2005
From: eharrison at mail.mesd.k12.or.us (Eric Harrison)
Date: Thu, 17 Nov 2005 21:45:03 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] dansguardian and K12LTSP
In-Reply-To: <437CDBD5.2090509@acm.org>
References: <437CDBD5.2090509@acm.org>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0511172124350.18113@k12ltsp.mesd.k12.or.us>

On Thu, 17 Nov 2005, Roderick A. Anderson wrote:

> At our last user meeting ( North Idaho Linux User Group - nilug.org ) we tried 
> to get dansguardian working with a k12ltsp server and thin clients.

First, you probably want to ask K12LTSP questions on the K12LTSP list...
https://www.redhat.com/mailman/listinfo/k12osn

> We would prefer having it all happen on the server without dealing with 
> configuring firefox and locking it down for each user.

Second, you can't have both thin clients and transparent proxying
on the same server. You need to keep the two functions seperate. [1]

http://www.k12ltsp.org/phpwiki/index.php/WebFiltering%3AIntegration


> Lots of searches and reading turned up conflicting information; from using 
> ipchains ( verses iptables ) to "it should work out of the box." None of them 
> worked.

K12LTSP is setup to do transparent proxying with squidGuard, but it is
easy to adapt it to Dan's Guardian. Make sure you have the squidguard
package installed, then edit /etc/init.d/transparent-proxying and
change the two references to "--to-port 3128" to "--to-port 8080".
Then start it up...

 	/sbin/chkconfig transparent-proxying on
 	/sbin/service transparent-proxying start


-Eric

[1] technically speaking it *can* be done on a single server, but that
     requires a non-standard iptables module & significant know-how.

From mwlist at gmail.com  Fri Nov 18 10:07:52 2005
From: mwlist at gmail.com (Mark Wills)
Date: Fri, 18 Nov 2005 10:07:52 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] VPN Server Information needed - Open VPN ?
Message-ID: <930d8d390511181007n33bf1c69h2ca84bb7ff120ddd@mail.gmail.com>

I'm looking for a "VPN server" for my work situation. Here's my wish list:
 Prefer open source solution.
Conect to and from both Linux and Windows computers.
Easy to use by end users.
 This means minimal set up issues by Windows end users trying to connect
from home to work.
Works through most peoples "firewall/routers" at home.
Authentication against Windows active directory would be great.
 I could live with a comercial appliance, but don't want to pay extra per
client.
I've seen some canned (netgear) "firewall/routers" that have built in VPN
but they appear to be optomized for a client that you have to pay a license
fee for every client machine.
 While open vpn (http://openvpn.net) doesn't seem to meet all the list
above, it looks interesting. Any body have any experience with it? Any other
products/projects come to mind?
 Thanks in advance for your help
 Mark Wills

This lets you VNC into it from any web browser anywhere.

From heinlein at madboa.com  Fri Nov 18 11:13:28 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Fri, 18 Nov 2005 11:13:28 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] VPN Server Information needed - Open VPN ?
In-Reply-To: <930d8d390511181007n33bf1c69h2ca84bb7ff120ddd@mail.gmail.com>
References: <930d8d390511181007n33bf1c69h2ca84bb7ff120ddd@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.64.0511181103120.3680@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Fri, 18 Nov 2005, Mark Wills wrote:

> I'm looking for a "VPN server" for my work situation. Here's my wish 
> list:

> Prefer open source solution.

> Conect to and from both Linux and Windows computers.

> Easy to use by end users.

The Linux 2.6 kernel series has a built-in IPSec implementation 
enabled in most distributions' kernels. It gets managed with the 
racoon(8) key-management daemon. Configuring the server side isn't 
trivial, but "road warrior" clients should work pretty easily.

See http://ipsec-tools.sourceforge.net/ for overall information and 
source code. See the Linux Advanced Routing & Traffic Control HOWTO 
(esp. chapter 7) for configuration details:

   http://lartc.org/howto/

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> www.madboa.com

On Fri, Nov 18, 2005 at 11:13:13AM -0800, Richard C. Steffens wrote:

> At this point, what I'd like to find out is whether the battery died, or

As always, it depends on how it failed.  If it won't run the computer
unless it's plugged-in, it's almost certainly the battery.

> and then whether I should replace the battery or the whole unit.

Even if you can find a replacement battery, a whole new UPS won't cost
much more, will have a warranty and will be safer.  Replace the whole unit.

> Can anyone recommend educational reading on the selection, care and 
> feeding of UPS's?

You can browse APC's site, but there really isn't much to do--plug it
in, test regularly and expect the battery to die after 2-5 years.

> OK. That takes care of the care and feeding part. How about the selection
> part. Other than manufacturer's sites, does anyone know of a site that

   Not really. But, UPSs are rated in VA units which are somehow different
from Watts. About 40 years ago when I had my Ham radio license, W=VA.
Regardless, VA > W in ratings. I believe the APC site has a table that shows
the wattage as well as the volt-amp rating.

> I recall measuring the current draw of my equipment some years ago, and I
> should probably do that again, since I've changed a number of things. But,
> other than that, and some idea of how long I want the thing to keep my
> machine running, are there any other things I should be thinking about?

   Have spare capacity. No guidelines, but enough so that you can plug in more
equipment in the future, or load up the boxes you have.

> Rich, I think you mentioned buying refurbished units. Did you say where you
> got them? Did they come with any warranties?

   No, I did not specify. I bought from RefurbUPS.com
<http://www.refurbups.com/> and am very pleased with the service and prices.
The unit I bought was the APC Smart-UPS 1400, for about the current $199.99
(plus a lot of shipping; it's heavy). That's rated at 950W/1400VA. They have
a Smart-UPS 1000 (670W/1000VA) and only 46 pounds instead of 58 pounds for
$179.99. They refurbish the electronics, put in a new battery, and test the
units before shipping.

   The apcupsd software works just fine with them.

From aaron at bavariati.org  Fri Nov 18 14:59:46 2005
From: aaron at bavariati.org (Aaron Burt)
Date: Fri, 18 Nov 2005 14:59:46 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] UPS Education
In-Reply-To: <437E4CC0.9010103@comcast.net>
References: <437E27C9.6080603@comcast.net>
	<Pine.LNX.4.63.0511181148540.21539@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<437E4CC0.9010103@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <20051118225946.GD18419@bavariati.org>

On Fri, Nov 18, 2005 at 01:50:56PM -0800, Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> >>Can anyone recommend educational reading on the selection, care and 
> >>feeding of UPS's?
> 
> >You can browse APC's site, but there really isn't much to do--plug it
> >in, test regularly and expect the battery to die after 2-5 years.
> 
> OK. That takes care of the care and feeding part. How about the 
> selection part. Other than manufacturer's sites, does anyone know of a 
> site that discusses the selection of a UPS?

Of course, there are manufacturer's sites, like the aforementioned
APC.  Their info is on the up-and-up, so look there.

Basically, a UPS has two ratings: VA* (how much power it can supply)
and battery life (for how long).  Add up the wattage ratings of all
the power supplies you'll be plugging in, then look at UPSes with at
least that VA rating.  Pick out one that'll supply somewhat more than
your wattage for at least 10 minutes or double your typical outage time.

Choose carefully what you plug in.  Network equipment-yes; monitor-yes;
speakers-maybe; inkjet printer-maybe; laser printer-no.

Single-PC-sized UPSes are available for <$100 at Office Despot these
days, but if you need cheap, FreeGeek has tested units at their store.

Good luck,
  Aaron


* VA is (peak volts)*(peak amps), about 1.4*Watts.  Given engineering
  tolerances and the fact that power supplies rarely operate at full
  load, there's some slack here.

Now that you mention them I recall that these are the basic criteria I 
used the last time I went through this exercise.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Fri Nov 18 20:05:08 2005

Subject: [PLUG] VPN Server Information needed - Open VPN ?
In-Reply-To: <437E5BBB.8050100@axpr.net>
References: <930d8d390511181007n33bf1c69h2ca84bb7ff120ddd@mail.gmail.com>
	<437E5BBB.8050100@axpr.net>
Message-ID: <20051119040508.GB7037@gate.kl-ic.com>

Mark Wills wrote:
> I'm looking for a "VPN server" for my work situation. Here's my wish list:

On Fri, Nov 18, 2005 at 02:54:51PM -0800, AthlonRob wrote:
> I've been using OpenVPN for a few years now and really quite like it.
> It's clean and simple, at least the way I'm using it. :-)

I am using OpenVPN to connect from my internal systems to my outside
virtual server - I have been running my mail and other services up and
down this pipe for two years.  The connection is reliable.  I don't
know about Windows, beyond the fact that a Windows-client to *nix
server is available.  Since the VPN connection is bidirectional, I
would always use a secure Linux machine as the server end;  if I
needed to connect two Windows boxes, I would connect them through
a more secure Linux server.  Opening an inbound port on a Windows
machine scares the water out of me.

I had a little difficulty setting it up, but that was mostly because
I didn't RTFM completely.  I could show you how to set up a simple
linux-to-linux link.

I am preparing a presentation on "virtual servers, virtual networks"
that I expect to present at one of the PLUG meetings.  This is your 
opportunity to push me along.
 
Keith

One solution I haven't seen mentioned yet is OpenSwan

Mark Wills wrote:
> I'm looking for a "VPN server" for my work situation. Here's my wish list:
>  Prefer open source solution.
> Conect to and from both Linux and Windows computers.
> Easy to use by end users.
>   
Can't answer this one, but I do see quite a bit of discourse about
connecting Windows based pc's.  It does support certificates

>  This means minimal set up issues by Windows end users trying to connect
> from home to work.
> Works through most peoples "firewall/routers" at home.
>   
NAT-T has been a part of since it's FreeSwan days.
> Authentication against Windows active directory would be great.
>  I could live with a comercial appliance, but don't want to pay extra per
> client.
> I've seen some canned (netgear) "firewall/routers" that have built in VPN
> but they appear to be optomized for a client that you have to pay a license
> fee for every client machine.
>  While open vpn (http://openvpn.net) doesn't seem to meet all the list
> above, it looks interesting. Any body have any experience with it? Any other
> products/projects come to mind?
>  Thanks in advance for your help

From athlonrob at axpr.net  Fri Nov 18 22:23:21 2005
From: athlonrob at axpr.net (AthlonRob)
Date: Fri, 18 Nov 2005 22:23:21 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] VPN Server Information needed - Open VPN ?
In-Reply-To: <20051119040508.GB7037@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <930d8d390511181007n33bf1c69h2ca84bb7ff120ddd@mail.gmail.com>	<437E5BBB.8050100@axpr.net>
	<20051119040508.GB7037@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <437EC4D9.9040105@axpr.net>

Keith Lofstrom wrote:
> I am using OpenVPN to connect from my internal systems to my outside
> virtual server - I have been running my mail and other services up and
> down this pipe for two years.  The connection is reliable.  I don't
> know about Windows, beyond the fact that a Windows-client to *nix
> server is available.  Since the VPN connection is bidirectional, I
> would always use a secure Linux machine as the server end;  if I
> needed to connect two Windows boxes, I would connect them through
> a more secure Linux server.  Opening an inbound port on a Windows
> machine scares the water out of me.

You don't need to open a port, though.  The beauty of OpenVPN's use of
UDP is that most stateful firewalls will see Windows-behind-the-firewall
trying to talk to VPS-out-in-the-internet and neither needs an actual
open-to-the-internet port.

My VPN server sits behind my firewall.  I'm not forwarding any ports to
it at all, and have linked up with networks set up similarly with it.
'tis quite interesting.

> I had a little difficulty setting it up, but that was mostly because
> I didn't RTFM completely.  I could show you how to set up a simple
> linux-to-linux link.

I worked off of examples a friend had set up.  He beat me to OpenVPN by
a month or two and has quite the network set up now.

> I am preparing a presentation on "virtual servers, virtual networks"
> that I expect to present at one of the PLUG meetings.  This is your 
> opportunity to push me along.

Ah, that should be interesting.  I've been doing virtual servers and
virtual networks for a while now... and was recently recruited by a CS
prof to do an "Independant Study" project next term setting up a
many-networks-in-a-box that boots off CD.  I haven't investigated it too
much, but am planning on using UMLs to represent systems on the networks
and bridging to emulate switches the UMLs "plug in to".

Rob

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Sat Nov 19 10:07:42 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Sat, 19 Nov 2005 10:07:42 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Hardware Woes

   I have problems with two hardware items and the response from each vendor
is underwhelming. I'm hoping to get suggestions from you folks on how to get
resolution.

   1.) Netgear VFS318 Firewall/Switch/Router/VPN gateway. This is a version-2
unit. It routes to/from the 'Net just fine, but the internal (host-to-host)
file transfer rate is 47KB/s maximum (on a 100MB/s Ethernet). When I plug the
hosts into a separate Linksys switch, and the switch into the Netgear, the
within-network transfer speeds jump up to 3-5MB/s. Ergo, there's a problem
with the Netgear.

   On 5 November I went to the Netgear web site, registered this unit, and
filed a support request. The unit is warranted for 5 years (according to
their web site). The web site also states that a response would be
forthcoming within 1-2 business days. Right.

   On 15 November I submitted a follow-up e-mail, then decided to give them a
call. A superficially-nice drone somewhere in the Indian sub-continent
confirmed that it had been 10 days with no response. He mumbled something
about the software not being under warranty (huh?), but that he would
escalate the request and someone would be in touch with me in 1-2 days. Sure.

   Here it is, four days later, and the silence from Netgear fills the office.
This unit cost me about $130 and I don't want to toss it, but it's not
working and I cannot get the company to make good on the warranty. Heck, I
cannot even initiate a conversation with their tech support people.

   I think that I'll try calling the President of Netgear on Monday. Anyone
have other ideas?

   2.)  Soyo KT600 Dragon Ultra Platinum Edition motherboard. Now 14 months
old. I bought it because it had good reviews on the Web, supported the Athlon
XP/3200+ processor, and came with $110 in rebates from Soyo. Rebates have
never been paid; that's a different issue.

   Last month, just after the 12-month warranty wore out, the system started
to hang. Locked up tighter than a drumhead. You'll recall a thread on this
issue on this mail list. I ran memtest86 and every test passed with flying
colors. This morning, I again tried to compile the 2.6.13.4 kernel and the
system screeched to a halt during the build of ../kernel/module.o.

   Last month I filed a request for support to Soyo's USA e-mail address. I
also wrote to the vendor. The silence from those two compete with the silence
from Netgear for my attention. What do you folks suggest?

   I'm thinking of ordering a replacement motherboard from Monarch Computing,
because they support AMD processors. If I can get a Soyo replacement, I'll
sell it or use it in a MythTV box for my fiancee.

   I've not had such bad service from hardware vendors before. I would like to
get these issues resolved but I'm out of fresh ideas.

Rich

From heinlein at madboa.com  Sat Nov 19 10:46:14 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Sat, 19 Nov 2005 10:46:14 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Hardware Woes
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511190948180.29600@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511190948180.29600@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.64.0511191034120.4445@arrowhead.local>

On Sat, 19 Nov 2005, Rich Shepard wrote:

>  I have problems with two hardware items and the response from each 
> vendor is underwhelming. I'm hoping to get suggestions from you 
> folks on how to get resolution.
>
>  1.) Netgear VFS318 Firewall/Switch/Router/VPN gateway. This is a
>      version-2 unit. It routes to/from the 'Net just fine, but the
>      internal (host-to-host)  file transfer rate is 47KB/s maximum
>      (on a 100MB/s Ethernet). When I plug the hosts into a separate
>      Linksys switch, and the switch into the Netgear, the
>      within-network transfer speeds jump up to 3-5MB/s. Ergo,
>      there's a problem with the Netgear.

My first guess is that one or more of your cards is having trouble 
with autonegotiation. You'll want to check the settings on both hosts:

$ sudo ethtool eth0

They should both report exactly the same duplex setting and, 
preferably, the same speed setting, e.g.,

   Speed: 100Mb/s
   Duplex: Full

If they don't, take a peek at the ethtool(8) man page to adjust things 
manually.

>  I'm thinking of ordering a replacement motherboard from Monarch 
> Computing, because they support AMD processors. If I can get a Soyo 
> replacement, I'll sell it or use it in a MythTV box for my fiancee.

I've only place one order with Monarch, so caveat lector...

The hardware I got from Monarch has been rock-solid; I've no 
complaints now that it's up and running. My complaint is two-fold:

1. It took the better part of a month for my system to ship, and
    Monarch never notified me of delays.

2. The system didn't ship with all the RAM we purchased and it
    six separate phone calls -- all initiated by me -- to get
    this situation resolved to my satisfaction.

My initial impression is that you'll get really good parts, but speed 
of response to customer inquiries is definitely not up to my 
expectations (and you'll carry *all* the burden of follow-up if 
something goes awry with your order).

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> www.madboa.com


From linux at frankhunt.com  Sat Nov 19 10:53:28 2005

I have seen problems with some network components when one end of the 
wire couldn't autosense the speed.  The resulting confusion looked like 
the symptoms you are experiencing.  You might see if you can "hard wire" 
the line speed on both ends.

To save expensive call-center support time, they're trying to push off

*providing* support that way, so all they do is ensure that their

But not to worry, the call-center folks are paid to follow the script
carefully and prevent you from using the precious time of the actual
support people, let alone incur the cost of a warranty exchange.

> 2.)  Soyo KT600 Dragon Ultra Platinum Edition motherboard. Now 14

Sorry.  If you were dealing with a nice, reputable manufacturer, you
might have a chance, but then if you were, you'd have paid twice as
much anyway.

> Last month I filed a request for support to Soyo's USA e-mail
> address. I also wrote to the vendor. The silence from those two
> compete with the silence from Netgear for my attention. What do you
> folks suggest?

Support experiences like yours have trained me to *always* call first,
and find a way to badger the first-line phonedroid into transferring
me to support.

If they say a tech will call you back, it won't actually happen unless
you make a couple of follow-up calls.

Oh, and if the phonedroid has trouble understanding me, I hang up and
try again.  Unpleasant experience shows I'd end up hanging up anyway,
and it saves me the time, frustration and anger.

In sum: call early, call often, take no BS.

Oh, and buy local when possible.  Face-to-face support is *much* better.

From gilmanhunt at comcast.net  Sat Nov 19 15:05:34 2005
From: gilmanhunt at comcast.net (gilmanhunt at comcast.net)
Date: Sat, 19 Nov 2005 23:05:34 +0000
Subject: [PLUG] vpn silliness
Message-ID: <111920052305.3392.437FAFBD000E289200000D4022070215539B029A08020E03040709@comcast.net>

I have an embarrassingly stupid question for y'all.

I'm writing from my inlaws' in Klamath Falls. Before I left, I had set up my linux box at home with Poptop and the netgear box with forwarding the Poptop connection. I had imagined that I would be able to connect to my server at home from my windows laptop and browse the network (map a drive and all that rot). 

I know I misconfigured something, because I had to redo it with a differnet IP address, but it led me into kind of a difficult place to describe.

My routing out from the linux box at home was not working; I was on a different subnet from the netgear box (because I found that my inlaws were on the same subnet as my home subnet (192.168.0.0) and I was getting an error about 'loopback detected.' So I ssh'd in and changed the ip assignments for poptop, and I could connect.

But as soon as I did, my laptop lost its connection for ICQ and I could no longer browse the internet. Which implies to me that the laptop was sending _all_ of its internet traffic over the PPTP connection home, which is not what I wanted; I just wanted to connect like it was a network, and if I browsed for machines on a 192.168.0.x address (which I'll change to 192.168.something.else when I get home), the computer would be smart enough to send only that traffic over the vpn connection.

Reflecting on the nature of PoPToP and PPTP, I think I may have chosen the wrong vpn solution; Is there some sort of configuration thing that would help me with what I'm trying to do?

Thanks as always.
Russ (YAR!)


From nsxfreddy at gmail.com  Sat Nov 19 15:18:52 2005

Date: Sat, 19 Nov 2005 15:18:52 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] vpn silliness
In-Reply-To: <111920052305.3392.437FAFBD000E289200000D4022070215539B029A08020E03040709@comcast.net>
References: <111920052305.3392.437FAFBD000E289200000D4022070215539B029A08020E03040709@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <c29537840511191518g1c0d3d92y44475a478229102@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/19/05, gilmanhunt at comcast.net <gilmanhunt at comcast.net> wrote:
> I have an embarrassingly stupid question for y'all.
>
> I'm writing from my inlaws' in Klamath Falls. Before I left, I had set up my linux box at home with Poptop and the netgear box with forwarding the Poptop connection. I had imagined that I would be able to connect to my server at home from my windows laptop and browse the network (map a drive and all that rot).
>
> I know I misconfigured something, because I had to redo it with a differnet IP address, but it led me into kind of a difficult place to describe.
>
> My routing out from the linux box at home was not working; I was on a different subnet from the netgear box (because I found that my inlaws were on the same subnet as my home subnet (192.168.0.0) and I was getting an error about 'loopback detected.' So I ssh'd in and changed the ip assignments for poptop, and I could connect.
>
> But as soon as I did, my laptop lost its connection for ICQ and I could no longer browse the internet. Which implies to me that the laptop was sending _all_ of its internet traffic over the PPTP connection home, which is not what I wanted; I just wanted to connect like it was a network, and if I browsed for machines on a 192.168.0.x address (which I'll change to 192.168.something.else when I get home), the computer would be smart enough to send only that traffic over the vpn connection.
>
> Reflecting on the nature of PoPToP and PPTP, I think I may have chosen the wrong vpn solution; Is there some sort of configuration thing that would help me with what I'm trying to do?

You probably need to tell the Windows PPTP connection not to send all
traffic over the VPN tunnel (the default).  It should be in the
advanced TCP/IP settings for the VPN connection.  Something like "use
default route for this connection" or some such.

Jason "answering Windows questions on a Linux mailing list" Martin

From linux at frankhunt.com  Sat Nov 19 15:40:41 2005
From: linux at frankhunt.com (fh hillsboro)
Date: Sat, 19 Nov 2005 15:40:41 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] UPS Education
In-Reply-To: <20051119012213.083B08F12@tinman.seitzassoc.com>
References: <20051119012213.083B08F12@tinman.seitzassoc.com>
Message-ID: <437FB7F9.7090802@frankhunt.com>

So, to continue this very interesting and informative training session, 
i got out my (not so?) trusty Radio Shack V-A meter and tested some of 
my systems to see what kind of current they draw.  Here's the results:
1 - an old 233MHz Dell box:  never saw above 1 Ampere
2 - a pretty old 2 processor X 800 MHz HP workstation:  never saw above 
2 Amperes
3 - a home assembled 2GHz system: never saw above 1 Ampere
4 - a Sony 24" glass monitor (really heavy!!):  also under 1 Ampere even 
on startup

These numbers seem a bit light to me.  Any comments?  I used the meter 
and associated inductive pickup/multiplier on the 10X setting for better 
accuracy.


-- 
Frank Hunt
Confused Linux Admin
General Nuisance
Web Weasel

Mark Wills wrote:
> I'm looking for a "VPN server" for my work situation. Here's my wish list:
>  Prefer open source solution.
> Conect to and from both Linux and Windows computers.
> Easy to use by end users.
>  This means minimal set up issues by Windows end users trying to connect
> from home to work.
> Works through most peoples "firewall/routers" at home.
> Authentication against Windows active directory would be great.
>  I could live with a comercial appliance, but don't want to pay extra per
> client.
> I've seen some canned (netgear) "firewall/routers" that have built in VPN
> but they appear to be optomized for a client that you have to pay a license
> fee for every client machine.
>  While open vpn (http://openvpn.net) doesn't seem to meet all the list
> above, it looks interesting. Any body have any experience with it? Any other
> products/projects come to mind?
>  Thanks in advance for your help
>  Mark Wills
>   

I wrote some instructions a while back on replacing a Windows VPN (PPTP) 
server with Linux:

http://poptop.sourceforge.net/dox/replacing-windows-pptp-with-linux-howto.phtml

This is probably the simplest way to implement a VPN, especially if you 
have a lot of Windows users.
~M

   Dan asked me to write about PLUG on our Wikipedia page. However, I don't
know enough to do a credible job. If you write to me off the list with
information on the history of PLUG (when it was formed, by whom, and why),
what activities have been sponsored and/or promoted by the group, and so on,
I'll be happy to edit it all and put together information that we'd be
pleased to see on that web site.

   What's the major attraction of PLUG -- to you? What has it provided? I know
that several in the group were instrumental in initiating the Linux in
Education project, and we spoke of putting on a linux festival ... until we
learned that commercial companies were in the same market and would make us
look like the amateurs we were. What else?

   I recall mail list subscribers from Belgium, the Phillipines, eastern
Canada, central Texas (Austin), and Boulder, Colorado. It may be safe to
write that we are the oldest linux/UNIX users group west of the Cascade
Mountains in Oregon.

   Send me the material and I'll put it together. If you want illustrations to
accompany the text, send that along, too. Of course, all this will go over
the .sig of David Mandel as Penguin-in-Chief of the group.

Rich

From linux at frankhunt.com  Sun Nov 20 08:17:04 2005
From: linux at frankhunt.com (fh hillsboro)
Date: Sun, 20 Nov 2005 08:17:04 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] UPS Education
In-Reply-To: <20051120031706.GK18419@bavariati.org>
References: <20051119012213.083B08F12@tinman.seitzassoc.com>	<437FB7F9.7090802@frankhunt.com>
	<20051120031706.GK18419@bavariati.org>
Message-ID: <4380A180.5010805@frankhunt.com>

I made the measurements from the system power cords. My meter uses an 
inductive pickup/multiplier thingie that plugs into the wall outlet and 
the device to be measured then plugs into it. There is a "figure 8" 
looking gizmo attached to a power cord with the inner circle of the 8 
being 1x the current and the outer being 10x. The meter then clamps into 
either of these "circles". I had to use the 10x scale to get any 
readings since even on the 6A scale, the readings were so low. If these 
readings are in a realistic range, then my math says I need a 600VA (5A 
x 120V = 600 VA). Allowing for some headroom, I'm considering something 
along the lines of the Minuteman PRO1100iE. It has enough capacity that 
I should be able to plug in 3 or 4 systems, the monitor (I'm on a KVM), 
and network components. It also has the "MINUTEMAN SentryII?" software 
which supports Linux, Windoze and other OS's.
Aaron Burt wrote:

>>>>> "fh" == fh hillsboro <linux at frankhunt.com> writes:

fh> I made the measurements from the system power cords. My meter uses
fh> an inductive pickup/multiplier thingie that plugs into the wall
fh> outlet and the device to be measured then plugs into it. There is
fh> a "figure 8" looking gizmo attached to a power cord with the inner
fh> circle of the 8 being 1x the current and the outer being 10x. The
fh> meter then clamps into either of these "circles". I had to use the
fh> 10x scale to get any readings since even on the 6A scale, the
fh> readings were so low. If these readings are in a realistic range,
fh> then my math says I need a 600VA (5A x 120V = 600 VA). 

If your inductive pickup loop encloses the entire cable (all three
conductors), then the net current in that bundle should be zero.  You
need to split the conductors out and enclose only one at a time.  I
recommend unplugging the cable before you start cutting though.

From linux at frankhunt.com  Sun Nov 20 12:07:33 2005
From: linux at frankhunt.com (fh hillsboro)

References: <20051119012213.083B08F12@tinman.seitzassoc.com>	<437FB7F9.7090802@frankhunt.com>	<20051120031706.GK18419@bavariati.org>	<4380A180.5010805@frankhunt.com>
	<86k6f3nltj.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <4380D785.5070904@frankhunt.com>

The inductive pickup gizmo is designed for and comes with the trusty 
Radio Shack V-A meter.  The "Inline Inductive Pickup.Multiplier" allows 
you to measure current when two or more wires are bonded together (power 
cord).  It also provides 10X readings for low current measurements.  So, 
I'm pretty sure that is not the problem.  I'm merely wondering if my 
observed readings are realistic.

On Sat, Nov 19, 2005 at 10:51:42PM -0800, Keith Lofstrom wrote:
> 
> Still putting together a system for my wife's office.  Next comes
> the printer - we need a black-and-white laser printer that occupies
> the smallest possible space.  Most vendors call 10x15 inches a
> "small footprint".  I would like to see a unit a lot smaller than
> that, perhaps something portable,  or else a unit with a front output
> that can fit in a stack on a shelf.

HP (and maybe others) makes a printer with vertical input and outbout
bins on top.  Might have a 12"x10" footprint.  Low-volume, no
Postscript.  But in your position, I'd find a way to stick a fairly
thin printer (such as one of those inexpensive, Linux-compatible and
fast Samsung models) under the desk.  IMHO printers don't provide
enough useful interaction to deserve desk space.


From llywrch at agora.rdrop.com  Sun Nov 20 16:44:54 2005
From: llywrch at agora.rdrop.com (Geoff Burling)
Date: Sun, 20 Nov 2005 16:44:54 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] A Plug for PLUG
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511191745180.5156@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0511201633050.1413-100000@joan.burling.com>

On Sat, 19 Nov 2005, Rich Shepard wrote:

>    Dan asked me to write about PLUG on our Wikipedia page. However, I don't
> know enough to do a credible job. If you write to me off the list with
> information on the history of PLUG (when it was formed, by whom, and why),
> what activities have been sponsored and/or promoted by the group, and so on,
> I'll be happy to edit it all and put together information that we'd be
> pleased to see on that web site.
>
I'm confused by this request. As the PLUG expert on Wikipedia (okay,
self-described; okay, I gave a presentation on it last summer), I have to
point out that there currently *is* a page about PLUG in Wikipedia. Dan
Haskel started it, & I kept it from getting deleted. (The short version
is that Dan was disgusted at how he was treated & left, while I argued
that there was no reason to delete the article & saved it; the long
version requires an in-depth understanding of Wikipedia politics & rival
philosophies, is admittedly boring, & no I won't explain it here.) And
from what I've seen over the last couple of years, more than a few
PLUGgers have participated in Wikipedia.

I just took a look at the article about PLUG on Wikipedia, & I didn't see
anything wrong with the article -- except that more could be written.
And anyone -- be they members of PLUG or not -- can add more information
just by clicking on the "edit" button/tab, type in what you want to add,
& after previewing your changes, click "save". It's actually quite simple
& you don't need a Ph.D. to do it; just a working connection to the
Internet.

So why exactly does this article need work? I'm not arguing the point: I
just want to know so I can help.

Geoff

Richard B. Shepard, Ph.D.               |   Author of "Quantifying Environmental
Applied Ecosystem Services, Inc. (TM)   |  Impact Assessments Using Fuzzy Logic"
<http://www.appl-ecosys.com>     Voice: 503-667-4517         Fax: 503-667-8863

---------- Forwarded message ----------
After many months of being "off-line," the WyattERP libraries have returned
to open-source!

At http://wyatterp.com

you can find an open-source toolkit for building your own database-driven ERP
applications in a simple scripting language (Tcl/Tk). Typical applications
only require 100-1000 lines of front-end code for a fully-functional GUI
application. Also offered is a tool (Wyseman) for managing and upgrading your
database schema authoring files. These tools are probably overkill for most
single-user environments, but great for small to moderate enterprise
solutions. The toolkit comes with several sample applications to get you
started and there is a free mailing list (see sourceforge page) if you have
questions getting them running.

Commercial support, training courses and more sample applications may become
available if there is a demand.

While a prior release of the toolkit is in full and complete use in our own
enterprise (about 25 integrated applications for about 50 concurrent users),
this newly released version is "beta" grade. So your feedback in shaking out
the bugs would be greatly appreciated.

Happy downloads!

WyattERP

Jim,

   I figured out the problem and fixed it. I think. Another file had been
editied by someone running on a Microsoft system so it had DOS cr/lf instead
of lf as a newline. Running that file through dos2unix seems to have sped up
all file saves within emacs.

From iconoklastic at yahoo.com  Mon Nov 21 15:15:50 2005
From: iconoklastic at yahoo.com (Robert Kopp)
Date: Mon, 21 Nov 2005 15:15:50 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Software for IP Web cam
Message-ID: <20051121231551.71129.qmail@web50614.mail.yahoo.com>

I thought that getting an IP Web cam might be a neat
way to avoid the compatibility problem, but I was only
partially correct. It is set up in Windows and can be
accessed by any OS after that, using its IP address. 

Although it is supposed to work with Linux, the
browser specified for Windows is MSIE with Active-X
controls enabled. When the program is invoked in the
Web browser with MSIE, one has the option of recording

From danielmyoung at gmail.com  Mon Nov 21 17:58:38 2005
From: danielmyoung at gmail.com (Dan Young)
Date: Mon, 21 Nov 2005 17:58:38 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] A Python Syntax Question
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511211733110.28343@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0511211733110.28343@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <2e42bd9b0511211758s4fc9de34o3500b761b12e668c@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/21/05, Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:
>    I've a Python beginner's question on referencing a separate module from the
> module that holds the application invocation code. I'd appreciate having a
> clue stick passed my way.
>
>    Here's the pertinent line in eikos.py:
>
> class Eikos(wx.App):
>    def OnInit(self):
>      wx.InitAllImageHandlers()
>      self.main = mainFrame(None)

Does eikos.py import the module?

I think you want to either call it as:
import <yourmodule>
...
self.main = <yourmodule>.mainFrame(None)

or

import * from <yourmodule>
...
self.main = mainFrame(None)

--
Dan Young

That's "from <yourmodule> import *"  Replace * with specific class or 
function names if you desire to be that explicit.

Yeah.  Python has several ways for you to import things into your 
namespace, but you do have to have some kind of import statement for 
almost anything.

How did you manage to get your program to exit without:

  import sys
  sys.exit(0)

?

On Sat, 2005-11-19 at 15:40 -0800, fh hillsboro wrote:
> So, to continue this very interesting and informative training session, 
> i got out my (not so?) trusty Radio Shack V-A meter and tested some of 
> my systems to see what kind of current they draw.  Here's the results:
> 1 - an old 233MHz Dell box:  never saw above 1 Ampere
> 2 - a pretty old 2 processor X 800 MHz HP workstation:  never saw above 
> 2 Amperes
> 3 - a home assembled 2GHz system: never saw above 1 Ampere
> 4 - a Sony 24" glass monitor (really heavy!!):  also under 1 Ampere even 
> on startup
> 
> These numbers seem a bit light to me.  Any comments?  I used the meter 
> and associated inductive pickup/multiplier on the 10X setting for better 
> accuracy.

Yup.  I recently played shepherd for a bunch of HP DL360s with dual 15k
RPM drives, dual 2.6GHz Xeon procs, lots of memory on metered APC PDUs
(power distribution units; think high-end powerstrip) and rarely saw a
draw of more than 6A with all 8 sockets in use (some of them were
plugged in but used by the secondary power supplies, which I was told
didn't draw if the primary was operational).

If my interpret my observations correctly, these high-power-draw servers
were only actually drawing about 100-150W.  If I'm wrong, I trust
someone who knows this stuff will disabuse me of these mistakes
(Galen?).

People seem to think that that 350W or 400W rating on the computer's
power supply indicates that it draws that continuously, like a
lightbulb.  That is not the case AFAICT, which is why UPSen are rated in
Volt-Amps instead of Watts--they are in fact the same, but VA is a
little consensual lie that makes you think about the actual draw, as
opposed to a power supply's rating.

I've been thinking about getting one of these, because I'm very curious
about this kind of thing: http://tinyurl.com/czjkx

Wil

> Yup.  I recently played shepherd for a bunch of HP DL360s with dual 15k
> RPM drives, dual 2.6GHz Xeon procs, lots of memory on metered APC PDUs
> (power distribution units; think high-end powerstrip) and rarely saw a
> draw of more than 6A with all 8 sockets in use (some of them were
> plugged in but used by the secondary power supplies, which I was told
> didn't draw if the primary was operational).

NOT the same


The measurement of electrical power that is computed by multiplying
volts times amps. In a DC circuit, volt-amps (VA) and watts are the same
because DC circuits do not add inductance and capacitance that take away
power. In AC devices, volt-amps ratings are higher than watts. For
example, in an uninterruptible power supply (UPS), the volt-amps rating
is approximately 60% higher than the actual wattage.



When a sinusoidal voltage is applied to a purely resistive load (an
electric heater) the current has exactly the same waveform and phase.
We use "rms" to indicate the magnitude of a sine wave voltage or current
because a sinewave of 120 volts rms produces the same amount of heat in
a resistor as a steady dc 120 volts.  A 120 volt rms sine wave has peak
values, plus and minus, of square root of two times 120, or plus and minus
170 volts.

For a purely resistive load, the power dissipated, in watts, is simply
volts rms times amps rms (watts == volt-amps).  Because then is no phase in DC.

If the load contains inductors (eg most motors or transformers), or 
capacitors, the current either lags behind or leads the voltage.  
Voltage and current are out of phase.  
When the voltage reaches its peak the current is not at its peak.  
If the difference in time between voltage peak and
current peak is given as an angle, theta (one complete cycle = 360 
degrees), then the power is volts rms times amps rms times cosine(theta).
Volt-amps is greater than watts.

When the alternating current supply is rectified to obtain the direct
current needed by most electronics, the current waveform may be far from
sinusoidal, for example "square-wave"-like or a series of impulses.
Here the power must be determined by calculating the product of the 
instantaneous voltage and current, and integrating the product over a full
cycle.   Watts will generally not be equal to volts times amps.

So, in sizing a UPS, make sure that the total load requires fewer watts,
AND fewer volt-amps than the rating of the UPS.  Unfortunately, most
devices do not have labels indicating both watts and volt-amps, so we
just have to guess, and use a somewhat larger UPS.





> 
> If my interpret my observations correctly, these high-power-draw servers
> were only actually drawing about 100-150W.  If I'm wrong, I trust
> someone who knows this stuff will disabuse me of these mistakes

> Volt-Amps instead of Watts--they are in fact the same, but VA is a

> opposed to a power supply's rating.

This is a good assumption...  The speed-o-meter on your car goes to 120
MPH...  How often do you go 120 MPH <OK.  Don't tell me.. I don't want
to know>


Then power supply manufacturer is assuming the user will draw at most
50% normal load....

Which means if you have a 400 Watt power supply  the PS vendor is
counting on you using only 200 Watts normally...

The PS is not designed to put out 400 Watts continuously.  
It can the life goes down rapidly!!!

Wil Cooley <wcooley at nakedape.cc> wrote:

> If my interpret my observations correctly, these high-power-draw servers
> were only actually drawing about 100-150W.  If I'm wrong, I trust
> someone who knows this stuff will disabuse me of these mistakes
> (Galen?).

Vram's explanation sounded good to me.  I'm really more of a digital
guy :-)   That said, I think your 100-150W number is reasonable.  Most
power supplies are rarely run at anything near their rated capacity.
The extra headroom is a good idea though.  Modern processors can go from
idle (<5W) to full tilt (> 50W) pretty much instantaneously.  System
power up can also tax the supply, particularly if drive spinup isn't
staggered.

galen

From seniorr at aracnet.com  Tue Nov 22 03:51:09 2005
From: seniorr at aracnet.com (Russell Senior)
Date: 22 Nov 2005 03:51:09 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] lots of coasters
In-Reply-To: <86sltpkmp1.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <86sltpkmp1.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <86lkzglx3m.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "Russell" == Russell Senior <seniorr at aracnet.com> writes:

Russell> I went to use a Ubuntu Live-CD (5.10) that I burned recently
Russell> and discovered that a band of sectors on it were bad.  Trying
Russell> to burn new ones resulted in the sectors being bad.  I've
Russell> burned on three different burners, one brand new, on two
Russell> different machines, all recent linux kernels (2.6.13.2 and
Russell> 2.6.14), two different brands of media, and get identical
Russell> failures.  The burning, executed as follows:

Duh.  Google finally decided to be my friend again.  I needed to add a
-pad or -dao option to my command line, then all is well.  md5sum
comes out fine, etc.  E.g.:

  # cdrecord -v -eject -dao dev=/dev/hdc /src_archive/ubuntu-5.10-live-i386.iso

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Nov 22 11:25:53 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 22 Nov 2005 11:25:53 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Cache usage and integer computation speed
Message-ID: <20051122192553.GA30877@gate.kl-ic.com>


This is more a computer science question than a Linux question, but 
there are probably folks in PLUG that can answer it.

I am working on an integer arithmetic problem that can be accelerated
with table lookups; for example, a randomly accessable 256Kbyte table
accelerates the computation by about 25 times.  Much larger tables make
the calculation somewhat faster, roughly proportional to the logarithm
of the table size.  I can make the table larger or smaller, impacting
compute time somewhat, but (I assume) impacting swap time and cache
misses significantly.  Overall program size is small, I/O is very
small, and the calculation is quite amenable to parallelization.  
It is not code-breaking, but it is that kind of intense arithmetic.

The calculation will run for a very long time on a lightly loaded
Linux machine with a P4 and a 512K cache.  I will probably use GCC
and a recent 2.6.X kernel, though I am told the Intel compiler might
give better results (debatable;  a separate question).

So the question:  what percentage of cache size should I target
my application and table to run in?  That is, how big can a chunk
of code and data get before performance starts to degrade?

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From creswick at gmail.com  Tue Nov 22 15:00:19 2005
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Tue, 22 Nov 2005 15:00:19 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Cache usage and integer computation speed
In-Reply-To: <20051122192553.GA30877@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20051122192553.GA30877@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <c834ec80511221500j2b1fbbb0td53b52bd17b66745@mail.gmail.com>

Disclaimer: I'm not really qualified to answer this, so everyone pipe
up if I'm wrong :) Basically, I'm looking to start a discussion here.

On 11/22/05, Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> wrote:
> So the question:  what percentage of cache size should I target
> my application and table to run in?  That is, how big can a chunk
> of code and data get before performance starts to degrade?

I doubt you'll be able to avoid cache misses*, but you can avoid
swapping by just counting your free memory at runtime and subtracting
your program's dynamic needs (including storage for output data.)

FWIW, your table could at least be a multiple of getpagesize() bytes
(4096 on my system).

* Eventually isn't it likely that even local (stack) variables will
end up in cache, and cause portions of your table to be relegated bace
to standard memory? Presumeably you won't be accessing every value in
the table more than anything else.. or will you?

--Rogan

> Keith

From griffint at pobox.com  Tue Nov 22 15:57:04 2005
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Tue, 22 Nov 2005 15:57:04 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Cache usage and integer computation speed
In-Reply-To: <c834ec80511221500j2b1fbbb0td53b52bd17b66745@mail.gmail.com>
References: <20051122192553.GA30877@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<c834ec80511221500j2b1fbbb0td53b52bd17b66745@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <4466.198.102.182.113.1132703824.squirrel@terryg.blindchicken.com>

> Disclaimer: I'm not really qualified to answer this, so everyone pipe
> up if I'm wrong :) Basically, I'm looking to start a discussion here.
>
> On 11/22/05, Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> wrote:
>> So the question:  what percentage of cache size should I target
>> my application and table to run in?  That is, how big can a chunk
>> of code and data get before performance starts to degrade?
>
> I doubt you'll be able to avoid cache misses*, but you can avoid
> swapping by just counting your free memory at runtime and subtracting
> your program's dynamic needs (including storage for output data.)
>
> FWIW, your table could at least be a multiple of getpagesize() bytes
> (4096 on my system).
>
> * Eventually isn't it likely that even local (stack) variables will
> end up in cache, and cause portions of your table to be relegated bace
> to standard memory? Presumeably you won't be accessing every value in
> the table more than anything else.. or will you?
>

If all that is wanted is to prevent the lookup table from getting swapped
to disk, just lock it in to memory with mlock(). See the man page for
mlock(2).

The problem course is that only root can do mlock(), so the process
would have to start out as root. After doing the mlock() the program
could setuid() to a non-root user for subsequent processing.

Terry

>
>* Eventually isn't it likely that even local (stack) variables will
>end up in cache, and cause portions of your table to be relegated bace
>to standard memory? Presumeably you won't be accessing every value in
>the table more than anything else.. or will you?

Correct me if I'm wrong, but isn't "which pages are in the CPU cache" 
determined by the kernel based on access frequency?  (and maybe some 
other interesting parameters)

If so, it would probably be a good idea to just use a (custom-ordered by 
frequency of use?) hash with buckets based on the pagesize (seems like 
there should be a lib for that.)  Yeah, you'll end up in main memory 
with some of the buckets, but if that performance hit is worse than 
just recalculating from nothing, then I have to doubt whether caching 
will actually give you real-world performance gains.

--Eric
-- 
But you can never get 3n from n, ever, and if you think you can, please
email me the stock ticker of your company so I can short it.
--Joel Spolsky
---------------------------------------------------
    http://scratchcomputing.com

less than positive, so why should I get another that may also fail in 13
months?

Subject: [PLUG] Post Thanksgiving Shopping Alert
Message-ID: <43873855.3010106@comcast.net>

Yesterday's Oregonian had a flyer from Office Depot. One of their 
coupons offered ink and toner for 50% off. While the words "Office 
Depot" are on the coupon, it is not clear from the way it's printed that 
the only products covered by the offer are Office Depot BRAND toner and 
ink. We learned this after waiting in line at the checkout counter. 
Fortunately, we were able to spot a new register opening that saved us 
another 20 minutes, but still, it was a waste of time to make the trip.

This was at about 6:30 this morning. When we entered the store, there 
were three lines with between 30 and 50 people in each line. Might have 
had something to do with the offer in the same flyer for an HP Presario 
laptop for about $350.

From seniorr at aracnet.com  Fri Nov 25 19:28:56 2005
From: seniorr at aracnet.com (Russell Senior)
Date: 25 Nov 2005 19:28:56 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] knoppix *hates* too much memory!
Message-ID: <86ek54f5on.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>


  "I must have put premium in this baby by mistake... it hates expensive gas!"

I've been working on a customized Knoppix CD again recently.  Since
the last time I did this, I upgraded the RAM in the box I am doing the
mastering on.  I noticed some weird instabilities, like getting cloop
errors reading blocks, and then swaths of applications not working
anymore.  Very strange.  I've done memtest86+ runs and they look
okay.  Usually I can get it to flip out by doing a "dd if=/dev/hdc
of=/dev/null bs=2048", opening/closing firefox a few times, etc.  I
just restarted with the "mem=1024M" boot option and things seem
better.  I've thrashed it around some and nothing strange has happened
yet.

BTW, I had been planning on trying Ubuntu's liveCD instead, because of
some weirdness with usb-storage handling in Knoppix, but Ubuntu, it
seems, has no practical way of fixing up video parameters.  It
insisted on running X at 640x480 despite ddcprobe clearly reporting
the correct (and much more capable) sync ranges for my monitor.  The
usb-storage handling is somewhat more sane on Ubuntu, but it didn't
seem like the tradeoff was worth it (all the configuration questions
at the front end was a bit tedious too).

From ehem at m5p.com  Fri Nov 25 20:24:26 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Fri, 25 Nov 2005 20:24:26 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] migrating to new uid/gid
In-Reply-To: <20051126033105.80810408A@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200511260424.jAQ4OQ3T088038@m5p.com>

>From: Vram <lamsokvr at xprt.net>
> On Fri, 2005-11-25 at 12:19 -0800, Galen Seitz wrote:
> > Russell Senior <seniorr at aracnet.com> wrote:
> > >   # find / -uid <uid>
> > > 
> > > etc?
> > 
> > That's really what I meant when I said recursive chown.  I'm just wondering
> > if the numeric uid/gid is hiding in any other files.
> 
> 
> In general users can only own files in 
> 
> /home/user
> /tmp/user
> 
> 
> Correct me if I am wrong...

Dead wrong. At a minimum add /var/mail and /var/tmp. Fairly often there
is /usr/tmp and /usr/local/tmp (fairly often linked to another tmp and
rarely used, but folks can create files there). In the general case using
`find` is highly recommended in order to guarentee you capture any extra
files.


>From: AthlonRob <athlonrob at axpr.net>
> Galen Seitz wrote:
> > I've got write permission to /usr/local.
> 
> Why would you do that?

Because it is handy. Things directly under /usr are generally considered
more secure than /usr/local. As /usr/local tends to be left out of $PATH
for SUID programs, the hazard from allowing it is not too large (doesn't
mean I do so though).

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Fri Nov 25 22:46:09 2005
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)
Date: Fri, 25 Nov 2005 22:46:09 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] grep and binary file response
In-Reply-To: <4387FF15.3040908@axpr.net>
References: <4387F514.2050501@mpcu.com> <4387FF15.3040908@axpr.net>
Message-ID: <438804B1.6060901@cesmail.net>

".bash_history", assuming you are currently logged on, is an open file 
and its buffers may not have been flushed. If you are interested in 
something in you history, use the bash "history" built-in. I believe if 
you are *not* logged in, you can grep in .bash_history and everything 
works just fine.

AthlonRob wrote:

>Keith Morse wrote:

>>grepping a binary file,  but .bash_history certainly not one.  Applying
>>a " -a " to grep works, but why should I have to?  Is there something in
>>the enviroment that would cause this behaviour?
